<td align=center valign=center colspan=2>
<b><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mike Huckabee<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor of Arkansas<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></b><br>State Capitol 
<br>Little Rock, AR 72201 <br>Phone: (501) 682-2345 <br>Fax: (501)

<table border=0 cellpadding=5>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td align=left valign=top><b>Vital stats 
<p>
<p>BORN:</b><br><TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>Aug. 24, 1955<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>, in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Hope<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/> 
<p><br><b>MARRIED:</b>
<p><TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Janet McCain<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> of Hope 
<p>
<p><b>CHILDREN:</b><br><TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>John Mark<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>David<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Sarah<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> 
<p>
<p><b>CAREER:</b>
<p><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>July 1996<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> - present <br>
<p><TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Lieutenant governor<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, 1993-96 <br>
<p><TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>President<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Cambridge Communications<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, Texarkana, Ark., 1992-96 <br>
<p><TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Pastor<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, Texarkana, 1986-92 and <br>Pine Bluff, 1980-86 <br>
<p>President, Arkansas Baptist State Convention, 1989-91 <br>
<p><TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>President<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>KBSC-TV<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> - 24-hour UHF channel, Texarkana, 1987-92 <br>
<p><b>ACADEMIC: </b>
<p><TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Hope High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, Hope, 1973 <br>
<p><TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Ouachita Baptist University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, Arkadelphia, 1976, magna cum laude 
(completed four-year degree in 2 1/2 years) <br>
<p>Attended <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Southwestern Baptist<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> <br><TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Theological Seminary<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, Fort Worth, 
Texas, <br>1976-77 <br>
<p><TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>Honorary Doctor of Humanities<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>, <br><TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>John Brown University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> 
<p>
<p><TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>Honorary Doctor of Laws<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>, <br><TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Ouachita Baptist University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/></p></td>
<td align=left valign=top>
<p>Mike Huckabee became governor <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>July 15, 1996<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>. As <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>lieutenant governor<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, he 
ascended to the office when the previous governor resigned. He became 
<TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>' 44th elected governor <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>Nov. 3, 1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>. 
<p>
<p>
<p><b>Achievements as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></b>
<p>Under Gov. Huckabee's leadership, <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>: 
<p>" Created ARKids First, which provides preventive and primary health 
insurance to children of working parents. 
<p>" Passed welfare reform measures that helped reduce welfare rolls by almost 50 percent. 
<p>" For the first time in state history saw a major, broad-based tax cut. 
<p>" Passed education reforms that encourage character education in 
schools, expand the availability of college scholarships, provide for the 
creation of charter schools and establish a new approach to workforce 
education. His new initiative, "Smart Start," emphasizes reading and math 
for students from kindergarten through the fourth grade.  'Smart Step' is a similar program for those in the fifth through eighth grades.
<p>" Passed the "Property Taxpayers' Bill of Rights."
<p>" Passed legislation that simplifies auto registration, previously a 
time-consuming enterprise. 
<p>"Began the largest road construction project in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> history.
<p>"Saw to it that all of the tobacco settlement money was devoted to improving the health of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansans<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.
<p>
<p><b>Other highlights</b>
<p>" In the fall of 1997, Gov. Huckabee released a book, "Character Is The 
Issue." The book, published by Broadman &amp; Holman, chronicles 
Huckabee's political career and discusses the importance of character in 
politics and life. 
<p>" His second book, "Kids Who Kill," was released in the spring of 1998. 
It addresses the issue of juvenile violence. 
<p>" His third book, "Living Beyond Your Lifetime", was released in 2000.
<p>" He served as chairman of the Southern Governors' Association in 1999-2000 and is now chariman of the Southern Growth Policies Board.
<p>" He was the 1997 American Sportfishing Association Man of the Year. 
<p>"He serves on the executive committee of the National Governors' Association.
<p>" He was inducted into the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Outdoor Hall of Fame in 2000.
<p>" His hobbies include fishing, hunting and playing bass guitar in his band, 'Capitol Offense'. 
</p></td></tr></tbody></table></body></html>

<td width=461 bgcolor="#FFFFFF" colspan=3><font face="Arial" size=4 color="#1E2A63">Biography</font></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width=461 height=10 colspan=3></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width=461 colspan=3><font face="Arial" size=2><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Win Rockefeller<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>, son of the late Governor Winthrop Rockefeller and grandson of the late John D. Rockefeller, Jr., was born in <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>September 1948<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>.
He attended <a href="http://www.pmb.ox.ac.uk" style="text-decoration:none"><TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Pembroke College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/></a>at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Oxford<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and is a graduate of the
<a href="http://www.ranch.tcu.edu" style="text-decoration:none">ranch management program</a>at <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Texas Christian University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>.
Rockefeller is the father of eight children. He and his wife, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Lisenne<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, maintain homes at Winrock Farms, in Conway County, and in Little Rock.&nbsp;<br>
<br>
Rockefeller was elected <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>lieutenant governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> in November 1996 in a special election when
<a href="/governor/" style="text-decoration:none">Mike Huckabee</a>assumed the office of governor after Governor Jim Guy Tuckers resignation on July 15, 1996. Rockefeller was elected for a full four-year term in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November 1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> after
receiving 67% of the votes cast.&nbsp;<br>
<br>
As <a href="history.html" style="text-decoration:none"><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>' lieutenant governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></a>, Rockefeller serves as the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>president of the<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>
<a href="http://www.arkleg.state.ar.us/" style="text-decoration:none"><TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Senate<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/></a>and as a goodwill ambassador for <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>
across the state and nation. He champions the issues of economic development and education. In 1997, he created
<a href="books.html" style="text-decoration:none">Books in the Attic</a>, a program using existing resources and volunteers to ensure access to reading opportunities for all children.&nbsp;<br>
<br>
Long before his election to public office, Rockefeller has been active in public
service. He is the immediate past president of the Quapaw Area
Council of the <a href="http://www.bsa.scouting.org/" style="text-decoration:none">Boy Scouts of America</a>and currently serves on the Boy Scouts National Board of Directors. He served from 1981-1995 on the
<a href="http://www.state.ar.us/asp/asp.html" style="text-decoration:none"><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> State Police
Commission</a>. In 1991, he was appointed by President George Bush to serve on the Presidents Council on Rural
America and was elected chairman. He has served on numerous boards, including the
<a href="http://www.tnc.org/infield/State/Arkansas/" style="text-decoration:none"><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Nature
Conservancy</a>, the <a href="http://www.acrc.uams.edu/" style="text-decoration:none"><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Cancer
Research Center</a>, and the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Arts Center Foundation. He is the founder and chairman of the board of the
<a href="http://www.billfish.org" style="text-decoration:none">International Billfish<br>
Conservation Foundation</a>.&nbsp;<br>
<br>
In addition to his public service, Rockefeller serves as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>chief executive<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of
<a href="http://www.winrockfarms.com" style="text-decoration:none"><TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Winrock Farms, Inc<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/></a>. and has interests in various small businesses
around the state in the areas of retailing, automobiles, farming and the resort industry. He is active member of the
<a href="http://www.nfibonline.com" style="text-decoration:none">National Federation of
Independent Business</a>.</font></td>
</tr>

<html>
<head>
<title><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>First Lady<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Janet Huckabee<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></title>
</head>
<body bgcolor="#85ACFB">
<center><table border=0 width=80%><tr><td align=center valign=center><a href="firstlady.html"><img src="janet1bt.jpg" border=0 alt="Inline Image" align=left></a></td><td align=center valign=center>
<h2><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Janet McCain Huckabee<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></h2>
<h4><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>first lady of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></h4></td></tr></table></center>
<br clear=left>
<hr>
<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Janet McCain Huckabee<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>, married to <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Governor <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Mike Huckabee<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, was born on <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>July 16, 1955<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>, in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Lake Charles, Louisiana<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>. <p>Having spent her childhood in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Hope, Arkansas<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/>, she graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Hope High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1973 and attended <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Ouachita Baptist University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in Arkadelphia, <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.<p>Mrs. Huckabee, along with her husband, share a priority in making meaningful contributions to the lives of families and children in the state of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>. She accomplishes this priority through several programs as first lady. 
<h3>Operation KidCare</h3>
To promote the health of children, Mrs. Huckabee serves as honorary chair of Operation KidCare in Arkansas and has traveled to all ninety-five health units in the state, emphasizing the importance of age appropriate immunizations of children. 
<h3>Smart Start</h3>
Working with this common sense initiative designed to give children a solid educational foundation, Mrs. Huckabee encourages parents to help prepare their children for success in school and life by reading aloud to them starting from the time they are infants.
<h3>Read to Feed</h3>
In the near future <TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>First Lady<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Janet Huckabee<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> will work with Heifer Project International's program "Read to Feed", giving children the opportunity to read, while also providing support and empowering others around the world to create a better quality of life.
<h3>Keep Children Alcohol Free</h3>
Mrs. Huckabee has associated herself with this national program, and plans, along with <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansans<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> for Drug  Free Youth, to conduct five teen summits on alcohol to help discourage underage drinking.
<h3>Rapid Response Team</h3>
The Rapid Response Team has been created in response to the numerous acts of violence that have occurred in schools across the nation and in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>, as well as the deadly natural disasters that have in recent times touched the lives of so many Arkansans. The first lady has helped train high school students in CPR, First Aid, AED, and Functional Disaster to assist when crisis occurs.
<h3>Habitat for Humanity</h3>
Mrs. Huckabee's involvement with Habitat has been on a multi-faceted level, from organization and fund raising, to the actual construction of the house. In the spring of 2001, she will wrap up the highly successful First Ladies Build program in which a home was constructed in each state, with the participation of the state's first lady or female governor, and will launch the next national , Women Build event, "Building a Legacy". 
<h3>Main Street Tours</h3>
In May, during <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Heritage Month, and in association with <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Historic Preservation, the first lady will complete a nineteen city tour with Main Street, a state and national program promoting the restoration of downtown historic buildings.
<p>
Janet and Governor Mike Huckabee have three children, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>John Mark<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>David<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Sarah<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>. In addition to her responsibilities as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>first lady of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Arkansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> and spending time with her family, Janet enjoys flying, hiking, camping, horseback riding, and swimming.
<hr>

</body>

<td>
<p><font face=verdana><b>BIOGRAPHY</b></font></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td height=15>
<p></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td valign=top>
<p><font size="-1" face=verdana><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Ruth Ann Minner<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>'s
election as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s first woman <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> is the
latest milestone in a remarkable journey - a
testament to hard work and determination and a true
<TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> story.</font></p>
<p><font size="-1" face=verdana>As <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Lieutenant
Governor<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> from 1993 to 2001, Ruth Ann led a
comprehensive review of state government,
spearheading changes in state agencies that made
them more efficient and customer-friendly. As chair
of the Interagency Council on Adult Literacy, she
led the expansion of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s adult education
network. And she worked to engage parents in their
children's schools, a key component to educational
success.</font></p>
<p><font size="-1" face=verdana>Ruth Ann's
service in the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> General Assembly is marked
with similar successes. As a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>senator<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> from 1982 to
1992, her most far-reaching accomplishment was the
<TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Land and Water Conservation Act. Over
30,000 acres of valuable land have been preserved
as a result of Ruth Ann's vision and desire to save
land for future generations. While a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>state
representative<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> from 1974 to 1982, Ruth Ann's
leadership was quickly recognized. She served as
House Majority Whip and as chair of the Bond Bill
Committee.</font></p>
<p><font size="-1" face=verdana>But it was as an
attach&eacute; and clerk in the state House of
Representatives and later as receptionist to
Governor Sherman Tribbitt that Ruth Ann got her
start in government. </font></p>
<p><font size="-1" face=verdana>Ruth Ann's
determination has seen her through personal as well
as political hardships. Born and a raised on small
farm <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>near Milford<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>, Ruth Ann left high school at age
16 to help support her parents and siblings. She
married <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Frank Ingram<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> and together they raised three
sons, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Frank Jr<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>., <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Wayne<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Gary<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>. Suddenly widowed
at age 32, Ruth Ann was left a single parent with a
family to raise. She returned to school - earning
her general equivalency degree and attending
college - and worked two jobs. Later, with her
second husband, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Roger Minner<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, Ruth Ann built a
successful family towing business. Roger succumbed
to cancer in 1991. The business is now owned by two
of her sons.</font></p>
<p><font size="-1" face=verdana>Ruth Ann's
greatest achievement and joy is her family - her
sons, her daughters-in-law and her seven
grandchildren. </font></p>

<h2 align=center><b>Biography</b></h2>
<p><blockquote>
<p style="margin-bottom: 6"><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>John Carney<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>'s election as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> is the next step in a long
career of public service in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.
<div align=left>
<table border=0 cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 width="88%">
<tr>
<td width="31%" valign=top align=left>
<p style="margin-top: 6; margin-bottom: 6"><img border=1 src="smallcarneyfamily.jpg" width=162 height=120 alt="Carney Family"></td>
<td width="69%">
<p>The second of nine children, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>John Carney<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was born in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Wilmington<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/> and raised in
<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Claymont<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/>. His father, Jack, was an administrator in the Wilmington Public
Schools and later the Brandywine School District. His mother, Ann, recently
retired following a long teaching career at Ursuline Academy.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<br>
<table border=0 cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 width="88%">
<tr>
<td width="66%" valign=top>John was a successful student-athlete at <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>St. Mark's High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, where he was
quarterback of the state championship football team in 1973. He graduated from
<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Dartmouth College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1978, where he was All-Ivy League and MVP of the football
team and co-captain of the lacrosse team. John came home to coach freshmen
football at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Delaware<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, while earning his <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>master's degree in
public administration<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>.</td>
<td width="22%" valign=top>
<p align=right><img border=1 src="smallfootball.jpg" width=137 height=115 alt="Football Picture"></td>
</tr>
</table></div>
<p><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>John Carney<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has more than 15 years of public service in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>. As the
state's <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Secretary of Finance<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, John continued <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s tradition of strong
financial management that helped the state earn a AAA bond rating. As a member
of the Cabinet Council for State Planning, John worked for resource preservation
and responsible economic development, securing funds to preserve the Inland Bays
and water resources statewide, to protect <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s farmland and open spaces,
and to invest in Wilmington's Riverfront. And, as chair of the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Center
for Education Technology, John Carney leads the effort to keep Delaware's
schools on the cutting edge of education technology.</p>
<div>
<table border=0 cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 width="88%">
<tr>
<td width="32%" valign=top><img border=1 src="smalljctc.jpg" width=173 height=125 alt="John Carney and Tom Carper"></td>
<td width="68%" valign=top>Before being appointed <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Secretary of Finance<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, John served as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Deputy Chief of Staff<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> to
<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Governor Tom Carper<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, where he was a member of the budget and finance team and
managed critical economic development efforts, including the state's purchase of
the Port of Wilmington. From 1989 to 1994, he was <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Deputy Chief Administrative
Officer<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> for <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>New Castle County<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, where his management responsibilities focused on
budget and finances, long-term planning, and public works. From 1986 to 1989, he
<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>served on the staff of U.S. Senator Joe Biden<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, and from 1984 to 1986, John
served as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Associate Director<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Catholic Youth Organization<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> in Wilmington.</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<br>
<div>
<table border=0 cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0 width="88%">
<tr>
<td width="67%" valign=top>In addition to his professional responsibilities, John has been an active
volunteer. He founded and coached in the boys' lacrosse program at St. Mark's
High School, and helped lead the development of the boys' lacrosse league in
<TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Delaware<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>. John also coached and mentored young athletes in Stormin' Norman's
basketball league. He is a member of the Board of Directors of the Delaware
Special Olympics, past president of the Triangle Neighborhood Association, a longtime member of the Board of the Catholic Youth Organization,
served on the Board of Goodwill Industries, and volunteered at the Emmanuel
Dining Room.</td>
<td width="35%" valign=top>
<p align=right><img border=1 src="seniors.jpg" width=192 height=150 alt="John Carney greets diner at Emmanual Dining Room"></td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>John lives in the City of <TAG name="RESCITY" value="start"/>Wilmington<TAG name="RESCITY" value="end"/> with his wife, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Tracey<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, and their two
sons, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Sam<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Jimmy<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>.</blockquote>

<td width=680 valign=top height="100%">
<table width="95%" border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=12 align=center height="100%">
<tr valign=top>
<td>

<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=3><b><font color="#666666"><img src="images/biography_hdr.gif" width=301 height=35></font></b></font></p>
<p><b><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2 color="#003399"><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> 
<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Roy E. Barnes<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></font><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=3 color="#666666">
</font></b></p>
<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1><img src="governor_pics/family.jpg" width=144 height=220 align=left vspace=12 hspace=12 border=1 usemap="#Map">
<map name="Map">


</map>
</font><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Roy 
E. Barnes<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was raised in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Mableton, Georgia<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> where he grew up talking 
politics and selling merchandise at his family's general store nestled 
between the highway and the railroad tracks in Cobb County. It was 
there - helping customers buy everything from fruit to work boots 
and swapping stories with neighbors - that Barnes developed his 
business sense and honed his populist touch. </font></p>
<p align=JUSTIFY><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>In 
1998, Barnes began his second run for <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, taking his message 
of education and healthcare reform to the people of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>. Though 
he was outspent two-to-one, Barnes won the election with 53 percent 
of the vote. On <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>January 11, 1999<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, he was sworn in as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s 80th 
<TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>.</font></p>
<p align=JUSTIFY><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>Barnes 
had two major legislative accomplishments during his first year 
as governor. He persuaded the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> General Assembly to create 
a transportation superagency, the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Regional Transportation 
Authority, with broad powers over transportation issues and urban 
sprawl. He also pushed through major healthcare reform legislation 
giving Georgians the protections of a Patients' Bill of Rights, 
allowing people to go outside their managed healthcare systems to 
choose their own doctors, and creating a consumer advocate to fight 
insurance rate increases.</font></p>
<p align=JUSTIFY><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>In 
his second year, Barnes focused on improving education. The education 
reform act which he signed into law on April 25, 2000 requires smaller 
class sizes and more accountability, provides merit pay for teachers, 
and gives parents, teachers, and principals more control over their 
own schools.</font></p>
<p align=JUSTIFY><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>Barnes 
is a lifelong legislator, lawyer, and businessman.</font></p>
<p align=JUSTIFY><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>After 
law school, Barnes became a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>prosecutor<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Cobb County district 
attorney's office<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>.</font></p>
<p align=JUSTIFY><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>In 
1974, at age 26, Barnes ran successfully for the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Senate, 
becoming one of the youngest legislators ever elected in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>. 
Within a few years, he was appointed to chair the Senate Judiciary 
Committee and became the Senate floor leader for then-governor Joe 
Frank Harris in 1983.</font></p>
<p align=JUSTIFY><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>While 
establishing himself in the Senate, Barnes built a private law practice 
in Marietta and began raising a family. In <TAG name="DOM" value="start"/>1970<TAG name="DOM" value="end"/>, he married <a href="http://www.ganet.org/governor/firstlady/"><TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Marie 
Dobbs<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/></a>, his college sweetheart. They have three children: <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Harlan<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, 
28, works for an Internet start-up company; <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Allison<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, 25, recently 
graduated from law school at the University of Georgia and clerks 
for a federal judge; and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Alyssa<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, 22, is entering the University 
of Virginia in the Fall of 2001 for her masters in special education. 
The family attends the First United Methodist Church of Marietta.</font></p>
<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>Roy 
Barnes first ran for <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> in 1990, finishing third in the <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>Democratic<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/> 
primary behind Zell Miller, who went on to win the general election, 
and Andrew Young. Barnes returned to the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> General Assembly 
in 1993 - this time to the House of Representatives.</font></p>
<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>Barnes 
graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>South Cobb High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1966, and then enrolled 
at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Georgia<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. In college, Barnes rebelled against 
his party roots, joining the Young Republicans in protest of the 
segregationist statements of some Georgia Democrats. (The corruption 
of the Nixon Administration later brought Barnes back to the Democratic 
Party.) He was also a member of the University's debate team.</font></p>
<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>In 
1972, Barnes received his <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>law degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>, cum laude, also from the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University 
of Georgia<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, where he was president of the student bar association.</font></p>
<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>Barnes 
was born on <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>March 11, 1948<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/> to Agnes and W. C. Barnes. </font></p>
<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=1>Since 
taking office, Barnes' personality and politics have won widespread 
praise. Dick Pettys of the Associated Press wrote that Barnes is 
&quot;a little bit like Tom Sawyer and a little bit like Clarence 
Darrow. But mostly, he's like the garrulous neighbor who swaps stories 
over the backyard fence - only funnier.&quot; In an editorial, The 
Marietta Daily Journal wrote, &quot;After they made Roy Barnes, 
they broke the mold. There just aren't many politicians and public 
servants with his populist touch any more. There aren't many who 
embody the Jeffersonian principle that government officials are 
the public's servants, not its masters.&quot;</font></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr valign=bottom align=center>

the Governor</a>&nbsp;<br>

<html>
<head>
<title><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>'s Biography</title>
</head>
<body bgcolor="#FFFFFF" link="#008000" vlink="#0000FF" alink="#808080" text="#000000">
<p>
<map name=map>

</map>
<a name=top></a>
<center>
<p><img src="images/biography.jpg" border=0 usemap=#map alt="biography header" width=600 height=88></p>
<p>
<table width=600 border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 align=center>
<tr>
<td width=600 valign=top>
<p><img src="images/portrait.jpg" width=200 height=259 align=right hspace=5 border=0 alt="Mark Taylor picture">
<p><a href="whatis.html">What is a <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>?</a></p>
<p><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>Born in 
<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Atlanta<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/> and raised in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Albany<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/>, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> is a <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> native son. In 
<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> defeated 12 opponents and carried almost 60% of the 
vote to become <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s 10th <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>. Lt. Governor Taylor 
campaigned on his successful 11-year career in the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> State Senate, 
where he served as Administrative Floor Leader for former Governor Zell 
Miller. In this role, Taylor sponsored the lottery-funded HOPE scholarship 
and pre-kindergarten programs &#150; programs that have provided over 
500,000 scholarships and over 400,000 pre-K places at no extra cost 
to taxpayers.</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>As 
Lt. Governor, and the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Senate's presiding officer, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> 
is working to accomplish his vision of more jobs, safer communities 
and better schools for all of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>In 
three legislative sessions as Lt. Governor, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has met with 
remarkable success, including passage of landmark legislation such as:</font></p>
<ul>
<li><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>a statewide 
<i>Student Code of Conduct</i>for <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s schools;<br>
</font></li>
<li><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>establishment 
of Special Drug Prosecutors in each judicial circuit;<br>
</font></li>
<li><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>a <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> 
Constitutional Amendment removing members of the General Assembly 
convicted of a felony from office;</font></li>
<li><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>the 
<i>Teen Driving Safety Act</i>to help save the lives of our young 
drivers; </font></li>
<li><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>the 
<i>Prevention of Corruption Act</i>streamlining the grand jury and 
indictments process against elected officials; </font></li>
<li><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>the 
<i>Crimes Against Family Members Act</i>targeting domestic violence 
abusers.<br>
</font></li>
</ul>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>Lt. 
Governor Taylor has worked hard to pass tougher teen driving laws and 
to revoke the licenses of teen drivers who commit moving violations, 
speed or skip school. Over the past three years <i><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s Teen Driver 
Responsibility Act</i>has resulted in over 70,000 teen drivers losing 
their licenses for violations &#150; undoubtedly saving thousands of 
lives on <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s highways. <br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>This 
year, Lt. Governor Taylor led the way in sponsoring and passing bipartisan 
legislation called the <i>Teen Driving Safety Act</i>. This new law 
incorporates strong, life-saving policies, including: mandatory drivers 
training, on-the-road exams for all new drivers, passenger limits, license 
suspension for moving violations and a 12:00 midnight to 6:00 a.m. driving 
curfew for 16 and 17-year-old drivers. <br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark 
Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has worked hard to reform <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s welfare system, sponsoring 
welfare-to-work legislation that has caused <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s welfare rolls 
to decrease by 65% and expanding statewide <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>&#146;s Wheels to 
Work program.<br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>Lt. 
Governor Taylor is a well recognized crime fighter and supporter of 
families. In 1999, he acquired funding for special drug prosecutors 
in each judicial circuit around the state, and he worked to pass the 
<i>1999 Crimes Against Family Members Act</i>, which increases the penalties 
against those who commit domestic violence in front of their children. 
<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> also championed <i><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s Two Strikes You're Out</i>
law, which incarcerates violent repeat offenders for life. <br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>In 
2001, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> passed legislation to establish an &quot;Electronic 
Protective Order Registry&quot; for all court-issued family protection 
orders. This registry will be available electronically to law enforcement 
prior to a domestic call-out situation to better enforce these orders 
and protect <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s families.<br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>In 
2000, the General Assembly passed Lt. Governor Taylor's proposal that 
requires every convicted felon in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> to submit a sample of their 
DNA to be analyzed and catalogued for law enforcement purposes. This 
has been touted as the most sweeping crime legislation to come out of 
<TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> in a generation and has already led to charges in dozens of 
previously unsolved sex and property crime cases. <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> believes 
that the accused, the victims and juries deserve to know guilt or innocence 
&#150; beyond a shadow of a doubt. This DNA &quot;gene&quot; print is 
doing exactly that. <br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>Lt. 
Governor Taylor is also dedicated to improving schools in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>. As 
part of his ongoing efforts to improve education, Taylor passed legislation 
that allows school systems to immediately and permanently suspend any 
student who physically assaults a teacher. This law builds on Taylor&#146;s 
1999 creation of a <i>Statewide Code of Conduct for <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s Schools</i>.<br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>As 
<TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lt. Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has also helped pass budgets containing $83 
million and $166 million in property tax cuts for <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s citizens 
as part of a program that will eventually exempt the first $50,000 of 
a home&#146;s value at no cost to local governments.<br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2>As 
a South <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> native, Lt. Governor Taylor makes economic development 
a top priority. Taylor chairs the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Rural Development Council, 
which is developing innovative state policies for helping rural <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> 
prosper. The GRDC's 2000 and 2001 legislative agendas met with great 
success in the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> General Assembly, an agenda that is helping hometown 
communities attract and keep jobs. Taylor also serves as vice chair 
of the OneGeorgia Authority, created to manage a $1 billion state investment 
in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s 71 poorest counties.<br>
</font></p>
<p align=left><font face="Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif" size=2><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mark 
Taylor<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> is a graduate of <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Emory University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Georgia 
School of Law<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. He has a teenage son, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Fletcher<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>.</font></p>
<p><a href="accomplishments.html"><img src="images/acc-btn.gif" width=119 height=19 border=0 alt=accomplishments></a>
<p><a href="#top">Back to the top</a>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</center>
<p>&nbsp; 
</body></html>

<td width=391 valign=top height=364><img src="images/1lady2a.gif" align=left>
<font size=+2 color="#666666"><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Marie Barnes<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> </font>married 
to <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Governor <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Roy E. Barnes<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, is a <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> native, born <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>June 13, 
1948<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/> in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Marietta, Georgia<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>, to Albert and Elizabeth Dobbs. She met Governor 
Barnes at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Georgia<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, where she received her <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in 
education<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>. They were married <TAG name="DOM" value="start"/>August 16, 1970<TAG name="DOM" value="end"/>.  
<p>&#9;Mrs. Barnes <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>taught elementary school<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> for two years, 
and her love for children has continued to be the focus of her volunteer 
efforts. She has developed a reputation for reaching out to help children 
in need, helping start afterschool programs and working with the March 
of Dimes. As <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>First Lady<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, she plans to work closely with programs dedicated 
to the health and welfare of children during the critical period from 
birth to three years of age. She currently serves as Honorary Chair 
for Safe Kids of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>, which focuses on accident prevention, and 
Georgians for Children, a children&#146;s advocacy group. </p>
<p>&#9;Women&#146;s health issues are also important to 
Mrs. Barnes. She has been asked to serve as the Honorary Chair of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>&#146;s 
Office of Women&#146;s Health, which will focus on education and prevention. 
In addition, she has assisted awareness campaigns for the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Chapter 
of the National Osteoporosis Foundation and the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Georgia<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Breast Cancer 
Coalition.</p>
<p>&#9;Mrs. Barnes is an avid tennis player and continues 
to play competitively in a local league. Governor and Mrs. Barnes have 
three children, all in their 20's.</p>

<p><img src="/gov/media/outdoor_closeup.jpg" width=118 height=179 border=0 name=photo alt="Dirk Kempthorne, Governor"></p>
</td>
<td width=9 valign=top align=left><img src="/gov/media/top_corner.gif" width=9 height=9 border=0 name="" alt=""></td>
<td valign=top>
<br>
<h3>Biography</h3>
<b style="mso-bidi-font-weight:normal"><font face="Arial" size=2>Career:<br>
</font></b>
<font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;Prior to being
elected as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Dirk Kempthorne<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> served for six years in the United
States Senate, beginning in January of 1993.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>In the 104<sup>th</sup>Congress, he wrote, negotiated, and won
passage of two major pieces of legislation:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>a bill to end unfunded federal mandates on state and local
governments, and a substantial revision of the federal Safe Drinking Water
Act.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span></font>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;In the Senate,
Kempthorne served on the Environment and Public Works Committee, where he
chaired the Drinking Water, Fisheries, and Wildlife Subcommittee.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>He also served on the Armed Services Committee, and chaired the
Personnel Subcommittee.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He
was also a member of the Small Business Committee.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;Governor Kempthorne
began his career in public service as the highly successful <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Mayor of
Boise<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In his seven years in
office, he helped direct a renaissance in the states capital city,
resulting in record growth, economic development and numerous national
honors and recognition for quality of life, business climate and family
issues.</font>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight:normal">Election
History:<br>
</b><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Dirk Kempthorne<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was elected as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>s 30<sup>th</sup><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> on
<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November 3, 1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, amassing 68 percent of the vote.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>He succeeded Republican Governor Phil Batt, and was inaugurated on
January 8, 1999.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight:normal">Accomplishments:<br>
</b>Declaring it the Generation of the Child, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Dirk Kempthorne<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>s first
two years in office have been marked by his efforts to ensure that <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>
children were healthy and well educated.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span></font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;Kempthorne established a
statewide voluntary immunization registry, to help ensure that more <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>
children from birth to 18 months receive the full complement of vaccinations
recommended by pediatricians.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He
also worked with the Legislature to enact an <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Reading Initiative, designed
to have every <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> child reading at grade level by the third grade.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;In 2000, the Legislature
approved his request for $873 million in state support for education  the
largest in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> history.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The
Governor has also begun an Innovative grant program for teachers who want to
offer their students exciting programs outside the normal curriculum.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;The Governor has
established a program to reward teachers who achieve National Board
Certification with cash stipends, and he has provided matching funds for the
states colleges and universities to attract and retain faculty.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;Kempthorne also stepped
up <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>s fight against the growing scourge of methamphetamine.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The Legislature approved his measure to establish tougher mandatory
sentences for those convicted of manufacturing meth, and he boosted the law
enforcement budget to provide advanced meth detection and interdiction training
for hundreds of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> law enforcement officers.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>In his first year in office, meth lab busts jumped by more than 70
percent.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;To provide the federal
government with a state-based solution for restoring salmon runs in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> and
the Pacific Northwest, Kempthorne established a Salmon Cabinet.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>This team of state officials is developing data and recommendations that
will help restore salmon in a way that will gather biological, political, and
economic support in the region.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His
efforts at building a regional consensus resulted in an historic bipartisan
agreement signed by the governors of the four Northwest states and presented to
the federal government as a roadmap to salmon recovery.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;To ensure that <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>s
diversifying economy continues to expand, Kempthorne has put forward initiatives
to foster rural economic development, more overseas marketing of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> products,
and greater integration of the states scientific, educational, and business
communities.</font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;In the spirit of
public-private partnership that helped establish the immunization registry,
Kempthorne has enlisted <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>s dentists in a voluntary program to offer
parents of all 2<sup>nd</sup>grade students free seal coating treatment to
prevent cavities in their childrens teeth.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span></font></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Arial" size=2>&nbsp;The Legislature
overwhelmingly approved Kempthornes proposal to establish the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>
Millennium Fund.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>This trust fund will receive proceeds from the national
tobacco settlement, and the interest earned by the fund will fund health
advocacy programs and other priority needs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Interest earnings are predicted to exceed annual payments within 20
years.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></font>
<td width=15 valign=top align=right><img src="/gov/media/spacer.gif" width=15 height=1 border=0 name="" alt=""></td>
</tr>

<td colspan=2 class="flHeader"><br>Biography</td>
<td width=195 valign=top><img src="media/crn_patricia2.gif" border=0 alt="Patricia Kempthorne" width=195 height=32></td>
<tr>
<td colspan=3 width=410 valign=top>&nbsp;
<p><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Patricia Kempthorne<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>, married to <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Governor <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Dirk Kempthorne<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> for <TAG name="YRSMARR" value="start"/>23
years<TAG name="YRSMARR" value="end"/>, grew up in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Boise, Idaho<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> and graduated from the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Idaho<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>
with a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in business management<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>. The First Lady's interests encompass
issues concerning children, families and communities and finding solutions
to the specific challenges they face, including parenting, education,
healthy life choices and work-life balance. She helped to found the Family
and Workplace Consortium in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>, which encourages and assists companies
in developing a family consciousness in practice and policy. In addition,
she has owned her own business consulting for employers on family and
work/life issues. In 2000 Mrs. Kempthorne joined Business Psychology
Associates, in Boise, as the Director of Work-Life Initiatives.</p>
<p>As part of the Governor's Generation of the Child initiative, she
serves as the co-chair of the Governor's Coordinating Council for Families
and Children and as a liaison for numerous boards and commissions.</p>
<p>Mrs. Kempthorne is a member of Leadership to Keep Children Alcohol
Free. The initiative has brought together 28 Governors' spouses in support
of a nationwide public education effort focused upon preventing underage
drinking, with a special focus on the 9-15 age group.</p>
<p>Mrs. Kempthorne serves on the University of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> College of Business
and Economics advisory board, is an honorary chair for the Boys and Girls
Club and the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> State Library Summer Reading Ambassador. She also
serves on the advisory councils of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Idaho<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Kids Count, St. Luke's Children's
Hospital and The Casey Family Foundation. She is on the board of directors
for the Boise Family YMCA and the World Sports Humanitarian Hall of Fame.
</td>
</tr>

<td colspan=5 width=600 class="flContent">&nbsp;<br>

<head>


<title>GRAVES Biography</title>
</head>
<body bgcolor="#FFFFFF" background="http://www.ink.org/public/governor/backgrounds/stone.jpg">
<center><img src="http://www.ink.org/public/governor/images/govframe.jpg" alt="Governor Bill Graves" border=0 naturalsizeflag=3 height=169 width=135 align=BOTTOM></center>
<center><table border=0 cellspacing=2 cellpadding=0 width="90%">
<tr>
<td>
<center><b><font size=+1><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>BILL GRAVES<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></font></b>
<br><i><font size=+1><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></font></i></center>
<p><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Bill Graves<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> is the 43rd <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>.&nbsp; The Governor was re-elected 
to his second term with the largest percentage of votes of any Governor 
in the nation, and the largest percentage of votes in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> history.&nbsp; 
He is the first <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>republican<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/> <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> re-elected in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> since 1962, 
and the states longest serving <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>Republican<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/> <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>.&nbsp; Governor Graves 
is a native of <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Salina<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/>, where he grew up involved in the family business, 
Graves Truck Line. 
<p>He earned a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in Business Administration<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Kansas Wesleyan University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>
in Salina and attended graduate school at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Kansas<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>.&nbsp;
Prior to his election as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, he <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>served two terms as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Secretary
of State<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>.
<p>Governor Graves emphasis has been on sound fiscal management, lower
taxes, quality education, reducing the size of state government and common
sense regulation.
<p>He currently serves on the Jayhawk Area Council of the Boy Scouts of
America executive board, as well as the board of trustees for <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Wesleyan
University and the Sunflower State Games, and is an alumnus of the 1985
class of Leadership <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.&nbsp;
<p>The Governor and his wife, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Linda Richey Graves<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, are the very proud parents
of 4-year old daughter, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Katie<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>.
<p>
<hr align=LEFT>
<center>
<h3>
The Governor at a Glance:</h3></center>
<li>
43rd <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, elected on <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November 8, 1994<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/></li>
<li>
Assumed office on January 9, 1995 (his 42nd birthday)</li>
<li>
Re-elected in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> with 73% of the vote, carrying all 105 counties in the
State</li>
<li>
Previously, Graves served eight years as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Secretary of State<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> -- first
elected in 1986 and re-elected in 1990</li>
<li>
Graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Kansas Wesleyan University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1975, with a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in Business
Administration<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/></li>
&nbsp; 
<p>
<hr align=LEFT>
<center>
<h3>
Memberships and boards:</h3></center>
<li>
Executive committee of the Jayhawk Area Council of the Boy Scouts of America&nbsp;</li>
<li>
Board of the Sunflower State Games&nbsp;</li>
<li>
Member of the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Chamber of Commerce &amp; Industry&nbsp;</li>
<li>
Graduate of the 1985 class of Leadership <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>&nbsp;</li>
<li>
Commander in Chief of the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Cavalry, a public sector-based recruitment
team&nbsp;</li>
<li>
Natural Resources Committee of the National Governor's Association&nbsp;</li>
<li>
Commander in Chief of the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Army and Air National Guards</li>
<p>

the Meet the Governor Page</a>

of the Governor and First Lady</a>

<hr align=LEFT></td>
</tr>

<td width=10 bgcolor="#FFFFFF" valign=top align=left><img src="images/topleft_arc.gif" width=6 height=7></td>
<td width=430 bgcolor="#FFFFFF" valign=top align=left class=bodytext>
<p><img src="images/bio.gif" width=106 height=32 border=0 alt="Biography"></p>
<p><b><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>GARY SHERRER<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></b></p>
<p><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>LIEUTENANT GOVERNOR<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> <br>
and SECRETARY OF COMMERCE AND HOUSING</p>
<p><b>The Lieutenant Governor At-a-Glance:<br>
</b>Family: Married; two children<br>
Spouse: <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Judy<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/><br>
Appointed: <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>July 18, 1996<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/><br>
Elected: <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November, 1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/><br>
Term Expires: January, 2003</p>
<p><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Gary Sherrer<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was appointed <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> by Governor Bill Graves 
on <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>July 18, 1996<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, and was elected to the office in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>. Sherrer is <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'
45th <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, and on July 21, 2000, he became the longest 
serving <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> history by serving 1,464 days in 
office. </p>
<p>In addition to his duties as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, Sherrer also serves 
as the Secretary of <a href="http://www.kansascommerce.com"><font color="#0000cc">Commerce 
and Housing</font></a>. As Secretary, he oversees the agency charged with 
fostering and promoting economic development and enhancing the availability 
of affordable housing in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>. </p>
<p>As Chairman-Elect of the <a href="http://www.nclg.org/"><font color="#0000CC">National 
Conference of Lieutenant Governors</font></a>, Lieutenant Governor Sherrer 
helps lead the professional association which represents the elected officials 
who are next in line of succession to the governors in the 50 states and 
five territorial jurisdictions. </p>
<p>Lieutenant Governor Sherrer also serves as the Vice-Chair of the Governor's 
Cabinet, Co-Chair of the Midwest Economic Development Cooperation Council, 
and he recently served as the Chairman of the Governor's Vision 21st Century 
Task Force. As Chairman of the <a href="http://www.ink.org/public/governor/vision/index.html"><font color="#0000CC">Vision 
21st Century</font></a>Task Force, Sherrer directed a group of nearly 
100 well-respected Kansans who made recommendations to the Governor concerning 
the refocusing of policies and strategies as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> enters the new millennium.</p>
<p>He was honored with the Emporia State University Distinguished Alumni 
Award in 1994 and the Emporia State University Award of Excellence in 
1995. In 1999, Lieutenant Governor Sherrer was selected for the national 
Henry Toll Fellowship Program, and in 2000, he received the Carl Perkins 
Humanitarian Award in recognition of his contributions to the improvement, 
promotion, development and progress of career and technical education.</p>
<p>Before beginning work for Governor Graves, Lieutenant Governor Sherrer 
spent the majority of his career in the financial industry and has always 
played an active role in the community. He is a founder of the Leadership 
<TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Program, and he created Leadership Wichita. </p>
<p>Lieutenant Governor Sherrer is a native Kansan who graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Topeka 
High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Emporia State University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. In <TAG name="DOM" value="start"/>1965<TAG name="DOM" value="end"/>, he married <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Judy Waller<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> 
of El Dorado, Kansas. They have two grown children - <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Stuart<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> of Wichita, 
Kansas and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Nancy<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> of Prairie Village, Kansas. </p>
</td>
<td width=10 bgcolor="#FFFFFF" valign=top align=right class=bodytext>
<p><img src="images/topright_arc.gif" width=6 height=7><br>
</p>
</td>
</tr>

<html>
<head>


<title><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Linda Graves<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> Biography</title>
</head>
<body background="http://www.ink.org/public/governor/backgrounds/stone.jpg">
<center><img src="http://www.ink.org/public/governor/images/ladyframe.jpg" alt="Photo of First Lady Linda Graves" height=169 width=135>
<br><font color="#000000"><font size=+2><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Linda Graves<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>, <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>First Lady of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></font></font></center>
<blockquote>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Linda Richey Graves<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>, married to Governor
<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Bill Graves<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, has made the well-being of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> children and their families
the cornerstone of her work as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>First Lady<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>.
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; She is the honorary chairman of Operation Immunize,
a nationally recognized, statewide effort to insure timely childhood immunizations,
and the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Breast and Cervical Cancer Initiative. Linda also is the
honorary co-chairman of the capital campaign for Exploration Place, a new
children's science and technology museum opening this spring in Wichita.
She served as co-chairman of the Governor's Task Force on Childhood Hunger
and is spokesman for K.I.D.S., the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Identification Sticker Program
promoting the use of safety seats.
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; In addition, Linda is a member of the board
of directors of the Youth Entrepreneurs of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>, the Shawnee Mission
Medical Center Foundation, KCPT public television and the Greater Community
Foundation of Johnson County. She serves as a director to the Unified Group
of Mutual Funds, Waddell &amp; Reed Funds, Inc., and Target Funds, Inc.
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Linda has led the effort to restore Cedar Crest,
the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> governor's residence, and has raised over $2 million in private
funds for the home. The <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Preservation Alliance honored her in March
2000 with their Award for Excellence, given annually to recognize exemplary
preservation projects in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Kansas<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Born in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Topeka<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>, she is the daughter of Ronald
and Florence Richey. She earned a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in history<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>, graduating magna cum
laude from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Oklahoma State University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. She is a member of Pi Beta Phi Sorority.
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Linda was awarded a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>law degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>, cum laude,
from the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Washburn University School of Law<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in Topeka. She then joined the
Kansas City law firm of <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Levy and Craig, P.C.<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, an 80-year-old firm specializing
in business law.
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Linda was honored to be the first woman admitted
to <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>partner<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in the firm. She holds an <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>honorary Doctorate of Law degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from
<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Baker University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. Linda met Governor Graves on a blind date in 1988 arranged
by mutual friends. They were married in <TAG name="DOM" value="start"/>1990<TAG name="DOM" value="end"/> and, in October 1995, welcomed
a daughter, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Katherine Preston Graves<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>..
<br>&nbsp;
<br>&nbsp;

<title><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Mike Foster<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>'s Biography</title>
</head>
<body bgcolor="#FFFFFF" background="../../images/seals/grayseal3.gif">
<table border=0 width="100%">
<tr>
<td width="24%"><img border=0 src="../../images/newgov.gif" width=169 height=185></td>
<td width="76%"><p align=center><font size=7>BIOGRAPHY</font></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div align=center>
<center>
<table border=0 cellpadding=0 width="94%">
<tr>
<td width="100%"><font face="Arial"><br>
<TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Murphy James &#147;Mike&#148;
Foster, Jr.<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was born on <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>July 11, 1930<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>, in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Shreveport, Louisiana<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Shortly thereafter, his family moved to
<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Centerville<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> where he attended public school as a child.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">
&nbsp;<br>
</span><br>
As a young man, he was involved in several extracurricular activities including the Boy
Scouts.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Attaining the highest honor and rank
of Eagle Scout is the one childhood accomplishment the Governor still cherishes and holds
dear.<br>
<br>
In 1948, he graduated from high school and enrolled at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Virginia Military Institution<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>After one semester at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Virginia
Military Institute<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, Governor Foster
transferred to <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Louisiana State University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, where he was a member of the Delta Kappa
Epsilon fraternity and the National Order of the Scabbard and Blade.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>During his years at <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>LSU<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, he pursued a Chemical
Engineering degree; however, in 1952, he graduated in Chemistry.<br>
<br>
After graduating from the university, Governor Foster joined the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Air Force<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> and served in
the Korean War.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>After returning home to
Franklin from the war, he began farming sugar cane and soon after formed <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Bayou Sale
Contractors<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, primarily as a means to keep his farm crew together in the off-season.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Additionally, the Governor has been a board member
of several local banks, a junior warden of St. Mary&#146;s Episcopal Church, the president
of the St. Mary Parish Farm Bureau, and a member of the American Legion.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Over the years he has accumulated the following
licenses:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>single engine, land and sea
multi-engine and instructor.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Also, he can fly
and is currently working towards his helicopter pilot&#146;s license.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Governor Foster exemplifies a true modern day
renaissance man.<br>
<br>
A life in politics never appealed to Mike Foster; however, in 1986, after &#147;becoming
frustrated with the non-responsiveness of state government,&#148; he ran for a seat in the
State Senate.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>After fulfilling two very
active terms in the Senate, then Senator Foster decided that he could get more
accomplished as governor.<br>
<br>
On <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>January 8, 1996<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, after mounting a successful campaign as a <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>Republican<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/> candidate,
<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>M.J.
&#147;Mike&#148; Foster, Jr.<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>, was inaugurated as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>&#146;s 49<sup>th</sup><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>
since the Louisiana Purchase in 1803.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His
remarks in his inaugural address reflect a political philosophy that he still honors
today:</font></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="100%">
<p align=center><font face="Arial"><br>
&#147;I
believe the people of our state must have the power to change
our state.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>
</span>I believe your values, your
voices, and<span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp; </span>your
votes must lead the politicians&nbsp;<br>
rather than the politicians
<span style="mso-tab-count:1">
</span>leading
you.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This is your state . . . now you must&nbsp;<br>
govern it.
<span style="mso-tab-count:1">
</span>My
job will be to see that you finally have the opportunity to
do so.&#148;<br>
<br>
</font></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="100%"><font face="Arial">
After a very successful first term, Governor Foster ran for a 2<sup>nd</sup>term and won
in a landslide in the first primary.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This was
the first time in many years that anyone has won the governorship outright without a
runoff election.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was inaugurated in
<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>January 2000<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> and this term will expire in 2004.<br>
<br>
When he is not running the state, Governor Foster enjoys spending his free time at his
home, <i>Oaklawn Manor</i>, in <TAG name="RESCITY" value="start"/>Franklin<TAG name="RESCITY" value="end"/>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>While
family, fishing and hunting occupy the bulk of his free time; his thirst for knowledge and
education has led him to take motorcycle and helicopter-flying lessons.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He has even started taking courses part-time at
Southern University Law School in Baton Rouge.<br>
<br>
Governor Foster is happily married to <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Alice Cosner Foster<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">
&nbsp; </span>He has two children, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Murphy J. Foster, III.<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, who is an attorney in Baton
Rouge, and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Ramelle Townley<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He also has<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>two stepchildren <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Paul<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Troy West<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, both
engineers, and many grandchildren.</font></td>
</tr>
</table>
</center>
</div>
