<head>
<title>Biography of Lt. Governor Blanco</title>
</head>
<body bgcolor="White">
<img src="ltgovbig.gif" alt="Lt. Governor Kathleen Babineaux Blanco" align=right hspace=10 width=200 height=269 border=0><font size="+1" color="Navy"><b><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Kathleen Babineaux Blanco<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></b></font>is serving her second term as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor of the State of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>. She was re-elected by an overwhelming 80 percent of the state's electorate. As the state's second-highest official she oversees the Department of Culture, Recreation and Tourism, which encompasses the offices of State Parks, State Museums, State Libraries, Film and Video, and Cultural Development and Tourism. Also under her auspices is the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Serve Commission and the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Retirement Development Commission. <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Serve oversees 64 national service projects across <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>, and involves more than 13,000 service volunteers. The Retirement Development Commission is dedicated to marketing <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> as a premier retirement state.
<p>
<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Kathleen Blanco<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has served the state with distinction since 1984, when she became the first woman ever elected to represent the people of Lafayette in the State Legislature. She served two terms before being the first woman elected to the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Public Service Commission. While on the PSC, she served as chairperson in 1993 and 1994. Then in 1996, she advanced to her current position. Since taking office, tourism in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Louisiana<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> has increased by 41 percent, representing growth not only in visitation, but in the hotel industry, air travel and in state park reservations as well. Her mission, along with many other economic initiatives, is to position Louisiana along with Paris, Rome and London as a top travel destination. 
<p>
The Lieutenant Governor has been married to her husband, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Raymond<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, since <TAG name="DOM" value="start"/>1964<TAG name="DOM" value="end"/>. They are the parents of six children and the proud grandparents of three. 
</body>
</html>

King, Jr.<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> is serving his second four-year term as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Maine<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s 71st <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>. Victorious in his
first bid for public office in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1994<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, King was reelected in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> by one of the largest margins of victory in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Maine<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s history. He is one of the only two <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>independent<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/> governors in the country.<br>
Born on <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>March 31st, 1944<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>, the Governor graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Dartmouth College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1966 and the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Virginia Law School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1969. In 1972 he became <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Chief Counsel to the U.S. Senate Subcommittee on Alcoholism and Narcotics<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in the office of then-Senator William D. Hathaway. In 1975 he returned to <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Maine<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> to <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>practice law<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> with the firm of <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Smith,
Loyd and King<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> in Brunswick. In the same year he began his almost 20 year-stint as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>host of the television show &quot;<TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Maine<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Watch&quot;<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> on the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Maine<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Public Broadcasting Network. In 1983 he became <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>vice-president and general counsel<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Swift River/Hafslund Company<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, an alternative energy development company based in Portland and Boston. Governor King founded and served as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>President<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Northeast Energy Management, Inc.<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> in 1989, a position he held for 5 years. The Brunswick-based company specialized in the development of large scale
energy conservation projects at commercial and industrial facilities in central and southern <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Maine<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.<br>
Governor King is married to <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Mary J. Herman<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>. He is the father of four sons: <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Angus III<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Duncan<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>James<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Benjamin<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, and a daughter, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Molly<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>.<br>

<td valign=bottom width=229 height=192 background="back.jpg"><img src="gifs/spacer.gif"></td>
<td rowspan=2 valign=top>
<table border=0 bordercolor=yellow cellpadding=10 cellspacing=0 width=100%>
<td width="5%">
&nbsp;
</td>
<td>
<center><img border=0 src="header2.gif" width=393 height=97></center>
<hr width="100%" noshade size=5 color="#000080" align=center>
<table border=0 bordercolor=orange>
<tr>
<td colspan=2 align=left>
<p>&#9;
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Bob Holden<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>s life is an affirmation of the American Dream.  Raised on a small rural farm and educated in a one-room schoolhouse, Holden fulfilled his lifelong aspiration on January 8, 2001, when he took the oath of office as <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>s 5
3<sup>rd</sup><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>.  As the first <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> of this new century, Holden urged Missourians in his inaugural address to put aside their differences and unite to make the 21<sup>st</sup>century <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>s century.   &quot;The goal of my adminis
tration is to unite all Missourians in forging a bright future that holds maximum opportunities for each of us,&quot; he said.  Holden believes that bright future can be found in a commitment to better education, improved health care access, a well-traine
d, highly skilled work force, and a strong multi-modal transportation system.</p>
</font>
<b>
<center>
<p>HISTORY OF PUBLIC SERVICE TO <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>MISSOURI<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/></p>
</b>
</center>
<font size=2>
<img height=222 src="index_files/govholden.jpg" width=173 align=right>
<p>&#9;Holden served two four-year terms as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>State Treasurer<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> before he was elected to the Governors Office in 2000.  During these years in the Treasurers Office, Holdens major responsibility was to manage the states $17 billion in annual revenues.  As 
<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>State Treasurer<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, Holden accomplished what no other chief financial officer of the state has ever done  earn <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> $1 billion in interest from investments.  Other major achievements include establishment of Dollar$ and Sense, <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>s first statewide
partnership between banks and schools to teach children wise money management practices, and MOST, a state and federal tax incentive program to help parents save for their childs post-high school education. </p>
<p>Holden began his career in public service in 1976 as an <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>assistant<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> to <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>State Treasurer Jim Spainhower<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>.  In 1983, he defeated an incumbent and was elected to the Missouri House of Representatives from the 136<sup>th</sup>District (Springfield).  He serve
d three terms, from 1983 to 1989.  During his tenure in the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> House, Holden served as chairman of the House General Administration Budget Committee, served on the House Budget Committee, and championed campaign finance reform.  He co-sponsored the 
Excellence in Education Act and was House co-sponsor of a bill that reorganized the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Department of Economic Development.  From 1989 to 1991, Holden served as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>administrative assistant<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in the St. Louis <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>office of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Congressman Richard Gephardt<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>
.     </p>
<dir>
</font>
<b>
<center>
<p>FAMILY BACKGROUND</p>
</b>
</center>
<font size=2></dir>
<p>Born in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Kansas City<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/> on <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>August 24, 1949<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Bob Holden<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> grew up on <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>a farm near Birch Tree<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> in south central <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.  In 1973, he graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Southwest Missouri State University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> with a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in political science<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>.  </p>
<center>
<img src="index_files/fam.jpg" width=350 height=239 align=right>
</center>
<p>Holden met his wife <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Lori Hauser Holden<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> from Aurora when she volunteered to pour iced tea at a Jim Spainhower event in 1982 and the following year they were married.  They have two sons, 11-year-old <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Robert III<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, born in St. Louis, and 6-year-old <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>John D<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, 
born in Columbia and named for one of the Governors favorite teachers.  Holden is dean of the American Legion <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Boys State Legislative School, serves on the board of Boys and Girls Town of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> and the Parents as Teachers program.  He also ser
ved in the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> National Guard.</p>
<p>Bobs parents, Lee and Wanda Holden, still work the Birch Tree family farm where Bob spent his boyhood. </p></font></body>
</body>
</table>
</td>

<head>
<title><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Joe Maxwell<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> Bio</title>
</head>
<body text="#000000" link="#0000AF" vlink="#0000AF" alink="#FFFFFF" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" background="JM%20images/backgrounds/capitol%20washout.jpg">
<div align=center><center>
<table width=500 border=0>
<tr>
<td><img src="JM%20images/staff%20photos/joe-color.jpg" alt="joe-color.jpg (10139 bytes)" width=227 height=285></td>
<td><p align=center><font face="AGaramond Bold"><font size=7><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Joe Maxwell<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></font><big><big>
</big><br>
<big><strong><em><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>'s Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></em></strong></big></font><br>
</big></td>
</tr>
</table>
</center></div>
<p align=center><img src="JM%20images/misc/feather_bar.gif" alt="feather bar" width=540 height=46></p>
<table border=0 width="100%">
<tr>
<td width="100%"><big><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Joe Maxwell<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> grew up on the family farm outside the small community
of <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Rush Hill<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/>. From a large family, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Joe Maxwell<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> understood at an early age the importance
of responsibility and obligation to one's family.</big><p><big>The farm crisis of the 70's
forced Joe and his brother from the farm into other vocations.&nbsp; As a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>rural mail
carrier<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, Joe continued his strong sense of responsibility and respect for
individuals.&nbsp; When he and his twin brother opened their own small business, Joe
treated each customer's problem the way he would want to be treated.&nbsp; It was the
right thing to do...the repeat business was just a welcome byproduct.</big></p>
<p><big>Service is the foundation of Joe Maxwell's philosophy.&nbsp; He served his country
in the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> National Guard<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> for twenty years and was called to active duty during the
great flood of 1993.</big></p>
<p><big>As a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>state representative<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, Joe earned the reputation for working long hours and
taking on tough issues, like welfare reform and health care.&nbsp; He served as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>senator<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of
the 18th District, representing an area that stretches across a dozen <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> counties in
the northeast region of the state.&nbsp; As <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>state senator<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Joe Maxwell<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> continued to fight
for issues vital to the whole state.</big></p>
<p><big>He sponsored the <u>Patients Bill of Rights</u>in <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>.&nbsp; Once more he
was ahead of the curve, and provided a blueprint for the nation to follow.&nbsp; This year
Joe again worked on HMO reform and small business health care.&nbsp; This past legislative
session he successfully passed the <u>Financial Exploitation Act</u>to safeguard our
senior citizens' financial savings.&nbsp; He also fought for tougher child protection laws
ensuring that <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> protects its most vulnerable citizens and saw the passage of his <u>Child
Protection Act</u>become law in July of this year.</big></p>
<p><big>Like most <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Missouri<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> families, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Sarah<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> and Joe Maxwell work hard to provide for their
children.&nbsp; Their two daughters, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Megan<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Shannen<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, serve as constant reminders that
<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Sarah<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> and Joe must strive every day to make this world a better place.</big></p>
<p><big>His vision of a better world for our children comes through in Joe's legendary
hard work, and his genuine love for people.</big></td>
</tr>

alt="Tour Executive Mansion" /></a></td></tr></tr><tr bgcolor="#333399" height="100%"><td valign="top" height="100%"></td></tr></table>
				</td>
				<td name="content" width="100%">
					<table width="500" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" border="0">
						<tr>
							<td valign="top" width="500">
								<table width="100%" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" align="left">
									<tr>
										<td colspan="2"><br /><img src="/images/Subpages/TitleMeetBio.gif" alt="Biographical Information" width="478" height="54"></td>
									</tr>
									<tr>
										<td width="30"><img src="/images/SubPages/space.gif" height="1" width="30" alt=""></td>
										<td>
											<p><img src="/images/home/picbiogov.jpg" align="right" hspace="6" vspace="0" alt="Photo of Governor Easley" width="131" height="128">Michael F. Easley's inauguration as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>North Carolina<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> follows nearly two decades of public service spent fighting crime, protecting children and the elderly, and standing up for working families. Easley, born in <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>1950<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>, is the first post-World War II &quot;baby boomer&quot; to be elected as Governor of North Carolina.</p>

											<p>Mike Easley was first elected to public office in 1982 when, at age 31, he became <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>District Attorney<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> for the 13th Judicial District in Brunswick, Bladen, and Columbus counties. He was one of the state's youngest district attorneys, and he used his youthful energies to battle drug trafficking and public corruption along the district's coastline, achieving one of the highest drug conviction rates in the state. Easley prosecuted South American drug kingpins and was recognized as one of the nation's top &quot;Drug-Busters&quot; by USA Today.  While serving as a district attorney, Mike Easley boldly ignored political threats and directed the prosecution of numerous corrupt public officials in his district.</p>

											<p>As district attorney, he developed the first Rape and Child Abuse Victim Assistance program operated out of a district attorney's office. He also worked with the General Assembly to create investigative grand juries, a tool he then used to prosecute major drug traffickers. In addition, he also helped to create the Fair Treatment to Victims Act.</p>

											<p>Mike Easley was elected North Carolina's <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Attorney General<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in 1992, recording the highest-ever vote total for any candidate in North Carolina. When he was re-elected to the state's top law enforcement position in 1996, Easley was again the state's top vote-getter, receiving nearly 60% of votes cast.</p>

											<p>Soon after taking office as the Attorney General, Easley waged an aggressive and high-profile fight against consumer fraud, using the tools of litigation, legislation, and consumer education to prevent North Carolinians from falling prey to scam artists. His efforts have resulted in a dramatic decrease in fraudulent telemarketing calls in North Carolina. In the wake of Hurricanes Fran and Floyd, Easley quickly initiated the pursuit and prosecution of home-repair scam artists.</p>

											<p>One of Attorney General Easley's first priorities was to restore meaningful punishment to North Carolina's criminal justice system. Working closely with members of the General Assembly, prison officials, judges, prosecutors, and local law enforcement, he successfully challenged the federal court order that limited the state's prison population. The removal of this prison &quot;cap&quot; has kept thousands of violent criminals behind bars. Combined with the state's structured sentencing law, this action has resulted in a doubling of the average time served by violent felons. During Easley's eight years as Attorney General, North Carolina's violent crime rate fell by 15% and its murder rate dropped by 21%. Easley also worked to impose alternative punishments and establish drug treatment courts for non-violent offenders, to institute a statewide &quot;Safe Neighborhoods&quot; program, and to give law enforcement officers better tools to fight violent crime.</p>

											<p>In his role as leader of the North Carolina Department of Justice, Mike Easley spearheaded efforts to reach a national tobacco settlement and played a pivotal role in brokering the $206 billion dollar deal&#151;the largest financial recovery in history. His efforts will bring an unprecedented $5 billion in revenue to North Carolina over the coming years. The settlement also promises to be a giant step towards bringing stability to the state's tobacco industry and tobacco farmers.</p>
													        
											<p>Attorney General Easley's legislative achievements have included pushing new laws through the General Assembly that created &quot;weapon-free&quot; state school zones, removed the spousal defense for rape, ensured &quot;truth in sentencing,&#148; attacked telemarketing fraud and predatory lending, and prevented youth access to tobacco products. He was also a strong advocate for the Victim's Rights Amendment, ratified by North Carolina voters in November 1996.</p>

											<p>While Attorney General, Easley also led the successful effort to create the nation's first Business Court in North Carolina in an effort to better serve the legal needs of businesses and provide an incentive to attract industry and jobs to the state. He successfully argued before the North Carolina Supreme Court the case that established the right of governments to provide targeted economic incentives to companies, enabling the state and municipalities more effectively to recruit companies and increase the number of good jobs in North Carolina.</p>

											<p>With the support of the state's leading environmental organizations, Easley recently reached landmark agreements with major hog producers to develop environmentally superior technologies to treat hog waste and better protect the state's rivers and streams.</p>

											<p>In recognition of his professional accomplishments, Easley has received several awards including the North Carolina Association of Black County Officials' <i>Humanitarian Award</i> and the North Carolina Chapter of the American Academy of Pediatrics' <i>Excellence in Public Service for Children Award</i>. Easley also received North Carolina Common Cause's <i>1999 Leadership in State Government Award</i> for his efforts to strengthen North Carolina's campaign finance reform laws and to maintain the state ban on corporate contributions to political candidates. In recognition of his public health initiatives, Easley received the <i>1998 Health Policy Award</i> from the state Heart and Lung Associations, and the Cancer Society.</p>

											<p>Mike Easley began his campaign for governor by vowing to continue his fight for working families: &quot;I am running for governor because I want to guarantee that the working men and women of this state&#151;the people who get up early, fight traffic, do the dishes, and pay the bills&#151;have a champion in Raleigh. They deserve someone who will speak frankly about the challenges facing this state and who will carry forward the progressive spirit that has been North Carolina's hallmark for the past 100 years.&quot;</p>
													        
											<p>Easley also pledged that his administration would be committed to uniting North Carolina and making sure every family can prosper in the New Economy: &quot;I am running for governor to make sure that North Carolina grows and that, as changes occur around us, our working families get a fair shake in the process and a fair share of the prosperity that comes our way. Every region and every citizen of North Carolina must be included.&quot;</p>
													                        
											<p>Born in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Nash County<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>, just outside Rocky Mount, Easley was raised on a tobacco farm, the second of seven children. His parents, Huldah and Alex, instilled in their children the importance of a good education and hard work. After graduating from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Rocky Mount High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1968 Easley received his <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>B.A. in Political Science<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of North Carolina<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1972 with honors.  In 1976, he earned his <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>law degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>North Carolina Central University School of Law<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, where his wife Mary now serves as a professor of law. He graduated cum laude from law school and also served as Managing Editor of the Law Review.</p>

											<p>Easley is an avid hunter and sailor and an accomplished woodworker. He and his wife <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Mary<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> have one child, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Michael, Jr.<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, age 16.</p>
											<p>
										</td>
									</tr>
								</table>
							</td>	
						</tr>	
					</table>
					<br />
				</td>
			</tr>
			<tr>

											<img src="/images/biophoto.jpg" width="120" height="135" hspace="0" vspace="2" border="0" align="left" alt="Photo of Beverly Perdue">A  former  <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>public school teacher<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>health care  professional<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, and   co-chair  of  the  Senate  Appropriations   Committee, <TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Beverly Perdue<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has been a key figure  in shaping   our  states  successful  mainstream  agenda  for educational  excellence; affordable, accessible  healthcare; sustainable economic prosperity; and targeted tax relief for North Carolinas families.</p>
											<p>Lieutenant  Governor Perdue comes into  the  second  highest elected office in our state having <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>served five terms in the Senate  and two terms in the state House of Representatives<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>. During  this time, she was consistently ranked  one  of  the most   effective  members  of  the  North  Carolina  General Assembly  and quickly gained a reputation for being  one  of the legislatures hardest workers. </p>
											<p>Her   successes  include  shepherding  through  the  General Assembly such innovative education measures as the Excellent Schools Act, the Safe Schools Act, and Governor Hunts Smart Start  initiative for early childhood development.  She  has also  worked tirelessly to improve the quality of  long-term care  for older adults and remains focused on expanding home health care opportunities.  Furthermore, having crafted  our states  balanced  budget since 1996,  she  has  earned  her designation as a fiscally responsible fighter for the  needs of our people.</p>
											<p>In  just  the  past  year,  Bev Perdue  received  the  North Carolina  Association  of Educators  President  Award,  the North  Carolina Nurses Associations Legislator of the  Year Award,  the National Association of Local Boards  of  Health Legislator  of the Year Award, the North Carolina  Community Colleges Faculty Association Legislator of the Year  Award, and  the  North Carolina Council of Womens Jean  H.  Nelson Distinguished Woman of the Year Award.</p>
											<p>Additionally, the North Carolina Division of Aging presented her  with the George L. Maddox Award given annually  to  the individual or organization in the state that has excelled in creative programming for older adults.</p>
											<p>As  Lieutenant  Governor, Bev Perdue will  continue  working hard on the issues that matter to North Carolinas families: prescription  drug cost relief for seniors,  more  effective schools  in every community, clean air and water, access  to technology, a government that treats businesses and citizens as  valued  customers, and ensuring that our law enforcement officers  have  the  tools necessary to  fight  crime  while making sure that our communities and schools remain safe.</p>
											<p>A  resident  of  Craven  County, Bev Perdue  has  two  sons, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Garrett<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Emmett<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>; two step-children, Robert and Charlotte. She  is married to <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Robert W. Eaves, Jr.<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>  The family home  is in <TAG name="RESCITY" value="start"/>New Bern<TAG name="RESCITY" value="end"/>.</p>
											<p>Lieutenant  Governor  Perdue holds a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>Ph.D.<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>  and  a  <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>masters degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>  from  the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Florida at Gainesville<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>,  and she  is ready to put her 14 years of experience in the state legislature to work fighting for an improved quality of life for all North Carolinians in this great 21st century.                              </p>
											<br />&nbsp;<br />

<html>

<head>
<meta http-equiv="Content-Type" content="text/html; charset=iso-8859-1">
<meta name="GENERATOR" content="Microsoft FrontPage 3.0">
<title>6-15-98 Governor's Biography</title>
</head>

<body bgcolor="#FFFFFF">

<p align="center"><font size="5" face="Wide Latin"><b>Governor Gary E. Johnson</b></font></p>

<p align="center"><font size="5">State of New Mexico</font></p>

<p align="center"><font size="2"><b>&quot;People Before Politics&quot;</b></font></p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><b><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Gary E. Johnson<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>: First Governor in the history of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>New Mexico<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> to be elected to two
four-year consecutive terms. He is a successful, self-made businessman, family man and
accomplished triathlete.</b></p>

<p><b>The Johnson Administration Goal and Priorities:</b></p>

<p>Governor Gary E. Johnson&#146;s goal is to <b>improve the quality of life</b> of all
New Mexicans by concentrating on four major priorities: 

<ul>
  <li><b><u>Improving education</u></b> by making it more accountable; </li>
  <li><b><u>Bolstering economic development</u></b> by reducing taxes and by building roads
    and infrastructure; </li>
  <li><b><u>Reducing crime</u></b> by building prisons and expanding juvenile prevention
    programs; and </li>
  <li><b><u>Improving government efficiency</u></b> by holding the line on state government
    growth and on the number of state employees.</li>
</ul>

<p>Governor Johnson has made a commitment to the <TAG name="EMPLOYER" value="start"/>state of New Mexico<TAG name="EMPLOYER" value="end"/> to offer the <b>best
product, best service at the lowest possible price </b>and he believes that his pledge of <b>&quot;People
before Politics&quot;</b> defines his administration. Governor Johnson is delivering on
that commitment and pledge. </p>

<p><b>Real Results Across the Board</b></p>

<p>Governor Johnson believes the highlight of his administration is the achievement of
what he calls, <b>&quot;Real results across the board.&quot;</b> He believes his
administration has taken a very balanced approach to improving state government and uses a<b>
&quot;common sense, business-like approach&quot;</b> to running state government.</p>

<p>Johnson went above and beyond his promises to stop any new tax increase and to prevent
the number of state employees from growing during his first term in office. Governor
Johnson signed legislation to actually <b><u>reduce taxes by more than $106 million
dollars</u></b> a year and he reduced the number of state employees by 6% or by around
1,300 employees.</p>

<p>&nbsp;</p>

<p><b>Economic Development</b></p>

<p>Governor Johnson believes that a business friendly state will benefit everyone.</p>

<p>In addition to cutting taxes to encourage economic development, Governor Johnson has
signed a $1.2 billion dollar highway improvement package to fix and four lane 500 miles of
roads throughout the entire state without raising taxes.</p>

<p><b>Government Efficiency</b></p>

<p>Governor Johnson believes one of his major legacies will be the implementation of
Managed Care for Medicaid during his administration. A Medicaid budget that had grown out
of control by approximately 600% over the past 12 years, was stopped in its tracks and was
reduced; and at the same time medical services for the poor were improved. </p>

<p>Governor Johnson has also held the line on the growth of state government to around 4%
after years and years of double digit growth prior to his taking office.</p>

<p>Under the Johnson Administration, Welfare Reform is taking place and that means those
who receive public assistance, yet <b>can work, will now be required to work.</b></p>

<p><b>Education</b></p>

<p><b>Governor Johnson&#146;s number one priority is to improve education in the state</b>.
While the governor signed legislation to give public school teachers their largest pay
raise in 16 years, and has invested over $300 million additional dollars a year to
education during his first term in office, the governor&#146;s <b>&quot;For the
Children&#146;s Sake&quot;</b> educational reform plan calls for: more accountability,
school choice through vouchers; and expansion of charter schools. Governor Johnson signed
an open enrollment bill intended to give students more choice. </p>

<p><b>Reducing Crime</b></p>

<p>Governor Johnson&#146;s leadership has resulted in the construction of two much needed
prisons in the state in order to help fight violent crime. The design, building, financing
and operations of the prisons are privatized and the daily costs per prisoner will be less
than in state run operations. Also, the costly federal Duran Consent Decree is in the
process of ending after 20 years of affecting the state&#146;s ability to run its prisons.
In the area of Juvenile Justice, prevention programs for children are being expanded and a
new juvenile corrections facility is being built.</p>

<p><b>Election History/Background:</b></p>

<p>Gary E. Johnson, a <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>Republican<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/>, was first elected to be the 26<sup>th</sup> <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor of
New Mexico<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November of 1994<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> and was re-elected in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November of 1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>. He says his
re-election is a <b>&quot;stick to your guns&quot;</b> affirmation of what his
administration has accomplished and of what more he wants to do to improve the quality of
life in New Mexico.</p>

<p>Prior to becoming governor, Johnson and his wife, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Dee<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, founded Big J Enterprises, a
successful, full-service commercial and industrial construction company still operating in
New Mexico.</p>

<p><b>Role Model/Athletic Firsts/Personal Goal</b></p>

<p>Governor Johnson, an accomplished triathlete, has enjoyed promoting physical fitness
while in office. He was the first governor to compete in the <b>&quot;Super Bowl of
triathlons- the Ironman in Hawaii.</b> Governor Johnson has also <b>ridden his bike five
times across the state of New Mexico</b> for over 2,500 miles in his effort to bring
awareness to fitness and litter clean- up during his annual &quot;Trek for Trash.&quot; He
has <b>run 25 miles in army boots and military fatigues</b> with a 35 pound pack on his
back through White Sands Missile Range to commemorate the Bataan Death March. And the
Governor has taken a<b> flying leap off a 10,000 foot mountain in New Mexico</b> to help
promote the World Hang-gliding Championships which were held in Albuquerque. </p>

<p>When he has completed his work for the state of New Mexico, Johnson has personal goals
to achieve that include <b>climbing Mount Everest.</b></p>

<p><b>Simple yet powerful rules for good living and principles of good government.</b> </p>

<p>Governor Johnson lives his life by simple yet powerful rules: <b>Treat others like you
would like to be treated; keep your word; always do more than you say you will; tell the
truth; and be on time.</b> Governor Johnson&#146;s principles of good government include:
Become reality-driven; always be honest; always do what is right and fair; determine goals
and a plan to reach them; those who ought to know what is happening -need to know;
don&#146;t hesitate to deliver bad news; be willing to do whatever it takes to get the job
done. </p>

<p>Birthdate: <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>January 1, 1953<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/></p>

<p>Spouse: <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Dee Simms Johnson<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/></p>

<p>Family: Married, one daughter- <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Seah<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, one son- <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Erik<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/></p>

<p>Education/Occupation: <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of New Mexico<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>B.S. Degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> (1976); <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Construction
Company Owner<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/></p>

<p>Elected: First governor in the history of the state to be elected to two consecutive
four-year terms. He was first elected to be the 26<sup>th</sup> governor of New Mexico in
November, 1994 and was re-elected in November, 1998. </p>

<p>Term Expires: January 2002</p>

<p>State Population: 1.7 million</p>

<p>State Budget: $3.1 Billion (General Fund)</p>

<p>Chief of Staff: Lou Gallegos</p>

<p>Media Contact: Diane Kinderwater</p>

<p>*11/98</p>

<p align="center">####</p>
</body>
</html>
ENDOFDOC

<head>



<title>Walter Bradley's Biography</title>



</head>



<body background="STOSeal2.jpg">
<a name="top"></a>

<table border="0" cellpadding="5" cellspacing="0" align="left">

<tr valign="top">
<td align="center" bgcolor="#00bba8">
<a href="ltgovbio.htm"><img src="pw431.jpg" width="60" height="60" border="0"><br>
<font face="arial narrow">Biography</font>
</a></td>
<td rowspan=28 Valign="top"><img src="lt_gov.jpg" width="318" height="523" alt="" align="right">
<h1><strong><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>WALTER   D. BRADLEY<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></strong></h1>

<h2><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>New Mexico's  25th Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/></h2>

<p>Walter Bradley grew up in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Eastern New Mexico<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> and is a graduate of <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Clovis High 

  School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and attended <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Eastern New Mexico University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. After leaving ENMU, Walter 

  started his career at <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Texas Instruments<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> moving to <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>National Chemsearch<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> both in 

  Dallas, Texas. He excelled in private business, receiving several awards and 

  quickly moved up the corporate ladder.</p>

<p>After coming home to New Mexico, Walter built from scratch a successful real 

  estate business. He is listed in both Who's Who of Finance and Industry, and 

  Who's Who in the West. His extensive business skills and success is due to his 

  strong beliefs in the entrepreneurial spirit. </p>

<p>Walter Bradley was elected Lieutenant Governor in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November 1994<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>. </p>

<p>As Lieutenant Governor Walter is &quot;President of the Senate&quot;. Walter 

  served in this same legislative body as a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>State Senator<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> from Curry County from 

  1989 to 1992. Due to his success in the private sector, Walter was picked to 

  sit on the important Economic Development and the Education Committees. </p>

<p>While in the Senate, Senator Bradley was recognized by the New Mexico Association 

  of Commerce and Industry with their highest legislative rating.</p>

<p>The Lieutenant Governor's expertise continues to help <TAG name="EMPLOYER" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>New Mexico<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="EMPLOYER" value="end"/>. He currently 

  serves on the New Mexico Space Commission Board, the New Mexico Border Authority, 

  NM Workforce Development Board and is Chairman of the Small Business Advocacy 

  Council.&nbsp; </p>

<p>As Chairman of the Small Business Advocacy Council, the Lieutenant Governor 

  has spearheaded legislative reform and eliminated regulatory roadblocks for 

  small businesses. </p>

<p>Walter's efforts to help New Mexicans have not gone unnoticed. He has received 

  numerous recognitions including:</p>

<ul type=disc>

  <li>2000 Leadership Beatification 

    Award, Keep New Mexico Beautiful</li>

  <li>2000 Mark Weidler Distinguish 

    Public Servant Award, New Mexico Petroleum Marketers Association. </li>

  <li>1998 Progressive Farmer Magazine 

    Man of the Year </li>

  <li>1997 Distinguished Leadership 

    Award, Albuquerque National Association for the Advancement of Colored People 

    (NAACP) </li>

  <li>1997 Distinguished Service Recipient, 

    New Mexico Farm &amp; Livestock Bureau </li>

  <li>1997 Outstanding New Mexico's 

    Small Business Supporter, New Mexico Small Business Development Center. </li>

</ul>

<p> Walter and his wife, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Deborah<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, were married in Clovis.  They lived and raised their four children, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Tige<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Lance<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Nicole<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Kristin<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> in Clovis until Walter's re-election in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1999<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> when they moved to Albuquerque. Lt. Governor Bradley and Debbie, are also the proud grandparents of their granddaughter, Alexis.</p>

<a href="#top"><img src="up.gif" width="41" height="41" border="0" alt="up button"></a>



</td>

</tr>

<META content="text/html; charset=windows-1252" http-equiv=Content-Type>

           <TR><TD height=36 width=130></TD> </TR>
		</TABLE>
        
		<TABLE border=2 cellspacing=1 bordercolorlight="#000000" bordercolordark="#000000">
        <TR><TD>	
            <a href="http://gov.state.nv.us"><img src="images/governorspge.jpg" border="0" width="131" height="26" alt="Click here to visit Governor Kenny Guinn's Homepage!"></a>
		</td></tr>
		<tr><td>
            <a href="bio.htm"><img src="images/biography.jpg" border="0" width="131" height="27" alt="Governor Kenny Guinn"></a>
		</td></tr>
		<tr><td>					
            <a href="sos2001.html"><img src="images/stateofthestate.jpg" border="0" width="132" height="26" alt="Governor Kenny Guinn's 2001 State of the State Address!"></a>
		</td></tr>
		<tr><td>		
            <a href="pr.htm"><img src="images/pressreleases.jpg" border="0" width="131" height="28" alt="Governor Kenny Guinn's Press Releases!"></a>
		</td></tr>
		<tr><td>			
            <a href="contact.htm"><img src="images/contactinfo.jpg" border="0" width="131" height="28" alt="Contact Governor Kenny Guinn"></a>
		</td></tr>
		<tr><td>			
            <a href="http://silver.state.nv.us"><img src="images/nevadahome.jpg" border="0" width="132" height="25" alt="Click here to visit the Official State of Nevada's Homepage!"></a>
	     </TD></TR>
		 </TABLE>
	  
	</TD>
    <TD width=520>
      <p align="center">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
	<IMG alt="" border=0 src="images/guinn1.jpg" width="350" height="254" >&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
      <FONT face="Arial, helvetica, sans-serif" size=+1><B>Biography</B></FONT> 
      <P>

    <img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">
<p>
    Guinn, <TAG name="AGE" value="start"/>64<TAG name="AGE" value="end"/>, spent his boyhood in the small,
    Central Valley town of <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Exeter, California<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> where he met <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Dema<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, his wife of <TAG name="YRSMARR" value="start"/>42 years<TAG name="YRSMARR" value="end"/>. He
    earned undergraduate and graduate <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degrees in Physical Education<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Fresno State
    University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and later obtained a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>doctorate in Education<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Utah State University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in
    Logan. The Guinns and their oldest son, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Jeff<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, moved to Las Vegas in 1964 where Guinn went
    to work for the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Clark County School District<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> as a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>planning specialist<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>. Within five short
    years, he was named <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Superintendent of Schools<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in Clark County and served with distinction
    in that position until 1978. During Guinn's tenure with the school district, his second
    son, Steve was born.<p> <img src="images/kgdema.jpg" align="right" width="300"
    height="281" border="0"><p>

	<img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">
    In his work for the Clark County School
    District, Guinn was recognized as an effective administrator committed to educational
    excellence at a time when the county was experiencing exponential student growth. His
    service to Clark County students was honored when Kenny C. Guinn Junior High School was
    named for him.<p>

	<img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">	
    In 1978, Guinn began applying his management
    skills in business as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Administrative Vice President<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> for <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Nevada Savings and Loan<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> in Las
    Vegas, which later became <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>PriMerit Bank<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>. At PriMerit, he quickly advanced through
    management ranks and, in 1987, was appointed as Chairman of the Board of Directors of the
    Las Vegas-based bank. Soon thereafter, Guinn was recruited to the energy business as the
    <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>President<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Southwest Gas Corporation<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> and eventually became Chairman of the Board of
    Directors of that utility in 1993.<p>

	<img src="images/reading.gif" align="left" width="230" height="309"
    border="0">
	<img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">
    In 1994, Guinn was recruited by the University of
    Nevada Board of Regents to serve as <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>interim president<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>University of Nevada-Las
    Vegas<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>. During that challenging year, he restored credibility to the university's
    prestigious basketball program as well as instituting administrative and policy
    initiatives to enable the school to continue its growing success as an ever-expanding
    urban university. His compensation was $ 1.00 and he donated the remainder of his salary
    to UNLV's student scholarship fund and other student activities.<p>
	

	<img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">	
    In addition to his one-year term at UNLV,
    Guinn served the state in leadership roles on a variety of committees and commissions,
    including the Clark County Community College Advisory Committee, the UNLV Foundation Board
    of Trustees, the White House Conference on Children and Youth, the Las &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
    Vegas Citizens Advisory Committee on Downtown Development, the Governor's Commission on
    Government Reorganization,&nbsp; the Metropolitan Police Fiscal Affairs Committee, the
    Nevada Educational Development Council and the Advisory Group for Civil Justice Reform.
	<p>
	

	<img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">	
    Guinn has also worked in his community in a
    variety of volunteer roles, ranging from involvement in the Boy Scouts and Pop Warner
    Football to the United Way of Southern Nevada and the Southern Nevada Independent Youth
    Athletic Association.<p>

	
	<img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">	
    In addition to their two sons, the Guinns have six grandchildren.
	
	<br><img src="images/spacer.jpg" width=15 height=5 border=0 alt="Space maker">	
	<center><img src="images/family.jpg" width="400" height="218" border="0"></center>

</B></FONT>

			<TABLE border=1 align=right width=150>
	</TR>
      <TR>
		<TH>
		<IMG alt="Lorraine T. Hunt, Lt. Governor, State of Nevada" border =0 src="lhunt.jpg" width="150" height="200" >
		</TH></TR>
		</TABLE>		<H3><I>Biography</I></H3>
		<H5><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Lorraine T. Hunt<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/><BR>
		<TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/><BR>
		<TAG name="EMPLOYER" value="start"/>State of Nevada<TAG name="EMPLOYER" value="end"/></H5>
		

		<P>
		<FONT size="-1"><B>
<TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> Lorraine T. Hunt moved to Henderson, Nevada in 1943 with her parents from Niagara Falls, New York.  Hunt graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Las Vegas High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and attended <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Westlake College of Music<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in Los Angeles, California.  She began her musical studies at the age of nine and embarked on her professional musical career at 19 when she started performing in Las Vegas, Reno and Lake Tahoe.
<P>
It was then that Hunt demonstrated her entrepreneurial ability by making her first real estate investment in a piece of desert land on the outskirts of Las Vegas.  Years later the investment led her into the world of business when she became <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>president<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> and <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>chief exective officer<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Perri, Inc.<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, a real estate and restaurant management company.  
<P>
Hunt's business acumen led her into government and legislative affairs as a small business activist as well as into community service.    
<P>
Whether it is a personal or business-related endeavor, Hunt is committed to the state of Nevada because it has given so much back to her.  Throughout the years Hunt has acquired extensive experience in small business and was awarded with Nevada's first Governor's <I> Award for Excellence in Business </I> in 1987 as well as being named <I> U.S. Small Business Advocate of the Year </I> in 1989.
<P>
Throughout her years in Las Vegas, Hunt has maintained significant involvement in statewide economic development.  Her background in the entertainment industry and tenure as vice-chair of both the Nevada Motion Picture Foundation and Nevada Motion Picture Commission has been integral to the expansion of the film industry in Nevada.  Hunt was also a founder of Continental National Bank and is now on the Community Board of Wells Fargo Bank.
<P>
Along with her business expertise comes vast experience and knowledge of the gaming and tourism industries.  Hunt served as chair of the Las Vegas Convention and Visitors Authority Board of Trustees, along with terms as commissioner and vice-chair of the Nevada Commission on Tourism.  Hunt also served as director of the Nevada Hotel/Motel Association. 
<P>
In addition to her ongoing commitment to a prosperous economy for Nevada, Hunt also participates extensively in community service.  Her involvement includes serving as president and Trustee of St. Jude's Ranch for Children, along with many other groups that she supports both financially and through volunteer activities.  
<P>
Prior to being elected lieutenant governor in 1998, Hunt served a four-year term as Clark County Commissioner.
<P>
Hunt and her husband, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Charles<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, have been married <TAG name="YRSMARR" value="start"/>33 years<TAG name="YRSMARR" value="end"/> and have three grown children, two grandsons and one granddaughter.
		</B></FONT>
		<TABLE border=1 align=center>
<TR>
<TD><IMG align=left src="4.gif" width="200" height="178">
<FONT size="-1"><I>    Lieutenant Governor Lorraine Hunt and her husband Charles (better known as "Blackie") Hunt.</I></FONT>
</TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>

<head>
   <meta http-equiv="Content-Type" content="text/html; charset=iso-8859-1">
   <meta name="GENERATOR" content="Mozilla/4.5 [en] (Win95; I) [Netscape]">
   <title>Governor's Biography</title>
</head>
<body text="#000066" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" link="#800000" vlink="#808080" alink="#FFFF00">
&nbsp;
<br>&nbsp;
<center>
<h3>
<TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>John A. Kitzhaber<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>, M.D. - Biography</h3></center>

<p><br><TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/><TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Oregon<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> John Kitzhaber was born in <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>1947<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/> in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Colfax, Washington<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>.&nbsp;
He grew up in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Oregon<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> and graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>South Eugene High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1965.&nbsp;
After graduating from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Dartmouth College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1969, he attended the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University
of Oregon Medical School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, earning a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>medical degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> in 1973.&nbsp; He <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>practiced
emergency medicine<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in Roseburg, Oregon for 13 years.&nbsp; Kitzhaber is
married to the former <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Sharon LaCroix<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> of Saskatchewan, Canada.&nbsp; They
have one son, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Logan<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, born in October 1997.
<p>Kitzhaber first ran for public office in 1978 and was elected to the
<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Oregon House of Representatives<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>.&nbsp; In 1980 he was elected to the first
of three terms in the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Oregon Senate<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> representing Douglas County and parts
of Jackson County.&nbsp; He was elected Senate President in 1985 and served
in that position until 1993.&nbsp; Kitzhaber was elected governor <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November
8, 1994<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, and was sworn into office January 9, 1995.&nbsp; He was re-elected
on <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>November 3, 1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> and inaugurated for a second term on January 11, 1999.
<p>As Senate President, Kitzhaber was recognized nationally for authoring
the ground-breaking Oregon Health Plan.&nbsp; He is credited both with
crafting the plan itself and for bringing together diverse interest groups
to pass the law, which took effect in February 1994.&nbsp; Kitzhaber also
received recognition for his many accomplishments in the field of environmental
stewardship, including the prestigious Neuberger Award given by the Oregon
Environmental Council.
<p>During his first term as governor, Kitzhaber oversaw the expansion of
the Oregon Health Plan, which reduced the rate of uninsured Oregon children
from 21 percent to eight percent.&nbsp; In addition, Kitzhaber's welfare
reform plan, known as the Oregon Option, has reduced the number of welfare
caseloads more than 50 percent, saved more than $200 million in the state
budget, and helped nearly 20,000 Oregonians find work.
<p>Preserving Oregon's environment remains a priority for Kitzhaber, and
during his first term he developed and implemented the Oregon Plan for
Salmon and Watersheds.&nbsp; This is a collaborative plan that encourages
federal, state and local government agencies to work with private landowners
to restore watershed health and recover endangered salmon species.
<p>Education and opportunity for Oregon's children also has been a centerpiece
of Kitzhaber's administration.&nbsp; He has fought for stable education
funding, implementing the Education Act for the 21st Century, increasing
investment in Oregon's colleges and universities, including freezing tuition,
and juvenile crime prevention.
<p>Kitzhaber is an accomplished fly fisherman and enjoys Oregon's wild
rivers.
<br>&nbsp;
<br>&nbsp;
<br>
<center>
<p><img SRC="images/fly.jpg" ALT="Fishing Fly" NOSAVE height=121 width=129 align=CENTER>
<p><img SRC="images/bluebar.jpg" ALT="Rule" NOSAVE height=5 width=90% align=CENTER></center>

   <META HTTP-EQUIV="Content-Type" CONTENT="text/html; charset=iso-8859-1">
   <META NAME="GENERATOR" CONTENT="Mozilla/4.04 [en] (Win95; I) [Netscape]">
   <TITLE>Governor's Personal Message</TITLE>
</HEAD>
<BODY TEXT="#000066" BGCOLOR="#ffffff" LINK="#800000" VLINK="#808080" ALINK="#ffff00">

<CENTER><IMG align=center alt="State of Oregon Seal" height =123 src="../images/letter_head.gif" width=124  NOSAVE></CENTER>
&nbsp;

<P></P><B><FONT size=4>
<P align=center><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>SHARON KITZHABER<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> - BIOGRAPHY</P>
<P align=center></B>&nbsp;</P>
<P><FONT size=3>Sharon Kitzhaber grew up in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Saskatchewan, 
Canada<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> and graduated in <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>physical therapy<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Saskatchewan<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 
1977.</FONT>           
       </P>
<P><FONT size=3>Sharon first worked in Hawaii as a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>physical 
therapist<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in 1977, then worked for a year in Geneva, Switzerland. She traveled 
Europe, the Middle and Far East, and the Mediterranean before returning to Maui 
in 1981. Sharon opened her first <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>private physical therapy practice<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in 1984, and 
over the next eight years, she developed, managed and sold a three-clinic 
physical therapy practice on Maui, Hawaii.</FONT>             
              
             
             
           
</P>
<P><FONT size=3>As the wife of <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Governor John Kitzhaber<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, 
Sharon has dedicated herself to working on behalf of Oregon&#8217;s children and 
youth. She is a founder and the honorary chairperson for the Oregon Safe Kids 
Coalition, which is part of a national organization aimed at reducing 
preventable childhood injury. She is also deeply involved in the prevention of 
teen pregnancy through an abstinence-based peer mentorship program called 
"STARS" (Students Today Aren&#8217;t Ready for Sex). Sharon is also a co-chair of a 
national initiative "Leadership To Keep Children Alcohol Free" aimed at reducing 
underage drinking.</FONT> </FONT>            
              
             
          
           
         
             
         </P>
<P><FONT size=3>Sharon is on the board of the Multiple Sclerosis Society 
of Oregon and also is a board member of the 
Oregon Ballet Theatre and the Oregon Health Sciences Foundation, and she 
serves on the Giving in Oregon Council. She is an outspoken advocate for the 
arts and is committed to enhancing young people&#8217;s access and experiences with 
the arts throughout the state.</FONT>   
              
             
               
           
</P>
<P></FONT><FONT size=3>In her private life, Sharon is an 
instrument-rated private pilot and the delighted mother of a son, 
Logan.</FONT></P>

<CENTER><FONT SIZE=+1></FONT>&nbsp;</CENTER>
