<p align="center"><img src="_themes/governor/alvrule.gif" alt="Horizontal Separator" WIDTH="300" HEIGHT="10"></p>

<h2 align="center"><!--mstheme--><font color="#330099"><img src="images/govtitle.gif" alt="govtitle.gif (16855 bytes)" WIDTH="210" HEIGHT="62"><br>
<img src="images/govname.gif" alt="govname.gif (14805 bytes)" WIDTH="452" HEIGHT="72"><br>
<em>Biography</em><!--mstheme--></font></h2>

<p align="center"><img src="_themes/governor/alvrule.gif" alt="Horizontal Separator" WIDTH="300" HEIGHT="10"></p>

<p><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>William J. Janklow<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was born in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Chicago<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>. His father was a prosecutor at the Nuremberg
war criminal trials, but when his father died, the Janklow family returned to mother
LouElla's hometown, Flandreau, South Dakota. At 16, Bill Janklow became a high school
dropout and joined the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Marines<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>. After serving in Asia during the Quemoy-Matsu crisis, he
returned home to South Dakota in 1960, married <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Mary Dean Thom<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, and enrolled for the fall
semester at the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of South Dakota<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. When college officials discovered he didn't
have a high school diploma, they wanted him to leave, but he talked them into letting the
first semester be a test. His grades were good and they let him stay. </p>

<p>After earning his <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>law degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> in 1966, Janklow started working in the legal aid program
on the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Rosebud Indian Reservation<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>. Soon he was the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>director of all legal aid<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> for <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>South
Dakota<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>, winning court cases and national awards. He has argued and won more cases in the
United States Supreme Court than any lawyer in South Dakota's history. He also lectured at
Harvard, UCLA and other universities on Indian law and criminal law. </p>

<p>Republicans drafted Janklow as their 1974 Attorney General candidate and he won with
66.7 percent, the highest percentage for any South Dakota Attorney General's race. </p>

<p>During his one term as Attorney General (1974-1978), Governor Janklow: </p>

<blockquote>
  <div align="left"><!--mstheme--></font><table border="0">
    <tr>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Kept his campaign promise &quot;to be a trial lawyer, not a politician,&quot; <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Stopped the atmosphere of violence that began with the 1973 Custer riots, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Won landmark decisions before the U.S. Supreme Court on Indian law and criminal law, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Cracked down on welfare fraud, drug abuse and white collar crime, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Upgraded the state crime lab, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Improved the state's criminal investigation agency, and <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Had the best criminal conviction record of any previous SD Attorney General <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
  </table><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">
  </div>
</blockquote>

<p>His achievements as Attorney General caused many Republicans to urge him to run for
Governor in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1978<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>. He won with over 56 percent of the vote. In <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1982<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, he was re-elected with
71 percent of the vote, the highest margin of victory in the history of South Dakota
gubernatorial campaigns. </p>

<p>During his first two terms as Governor (1979-1987), Bill Janklow: </p>

<blockquote>
  <div align="left"><!--mstheme--></font><table border="0">
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Kept his campaign promise of &quot;Putting Taxpayers First,&quot; <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Reduced the state government bureaucracy by almost ten percent, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Managed state agencies so efficiently that over $50 million was returned to the state
      treasury, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Caused enough savings that he was able to fully fund a $40 million personal property
      tax repeal for the taxpayers with only $12 million in state sales tax broadening, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Saved SD's railroad system so farmers could have better access to Asian/European
      markets, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">More than doubled state aid to education to help hold down local property tax
      increases, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Prevented the budget crisis that occurred in over 30 other states in 1981 by seeing it
      coming and reducing state spending the previous August, 1980,<!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Won dramatic changes in state banking laws that caused a national revolution in
      financial services and created thousands of new jobs, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Accelerated development of Missouri River recreational and tourism opportunities, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Created more new plant expansions, more new industries and more new capital investment
      in South Dakota in his eight years than had been done in the previous twelve years at a
      time when federal policies were causing record-breaking years of high interest rates and
      inflation, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Started water development moving forward with the state's first water development plan
      and regular funding, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Dramatically increased the availability of capital for home loans so that the dream of
      home<br>
      ownership was realized by thousands of South Dakotans, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Implemented many joint agreements with Indian tribes so that they could have the
      opportunity<br>
      to manage their own affairs, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Creatively used prison labor for state fairgrounds rebuilding and many other projects,
      <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Implemented a rural renaissance program and computerized farm management courses, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Saved the Unemployment Insurance Tax fund from insolvency so that South Dakota became
      one of only 12 states who didn't need federal funding, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Transformed a small state college campus into a prison, thereby saving taxpayers $20
      to $40 million in new prison costs, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Reduced Medicaid fraud and abuse, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Substantially reduced alcohol-related accidents and deaths through tougher law
      enforcement, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Accelerated the transfer of children from foster care to adoption, <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Transformed a mismanaged state-owned cement plant from having lost over $70,000,000 in
      potential business and overspent $10 million in plant renovations to an efficient
      operation that deposited over $91 million in profits into the state treasury that didn't
      have to be raised in taxes, and <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td valign="top"><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica"><img src="_themes/governor/ablbull1.gif" alt="List Bullet" WIDTH="16" HEIGHT="16"><!--mstheme--></font></td>
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">Safeguarded the underground water supply of western South Dakota and received $5
      million from the ETSI Corporation for water development. <!--mstheme--></font></td>
    </tr>
  </table><!--mstheme--><font face="arial, Arial, Helvetica">
  </div>
</blockquote>

<p>After eight years in private life, Janklow was re-elected in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1994<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> to his third term as
Governor. He has often said that being Governor for the great people of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>South Dakota<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> is
the best job, the most challenging job, and the most enjoyable job that anyone could ever
have.</p>

<p><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> Bill Janklow began 1995 by winning legislative approval for the largest tax
decrease in South Dakota history and the largest tax decrease of all fifty states for
1995. Property taxes on agricultural land and owner-occupied homes were reduced by twenty
percent. Instead of allowing property taxes to increase at the recent average rate of over
$40 million per year, Janklow reduced property taxes by $83 million in his first year.</p>

<p>To stop large property tax increases at the local level, Janklow's tax reduction plan
also limits local government and school spending to annual increases of only three percent
or inflation, whichever is lower. Janklow also put the same tight budget controls on state
government by keeping the state spending under the rate of inflation for the first time in
eight years. </p>

<p>In 1996, Janklow's budget for state government is the first one since the Great
Depression that actually spends less money than the previous year. It contains a reduction
of over 790 people and since the budget's approval, Janklow has eliminated another 250
jobs. Janklow has reduced the part of state government he supervises by over ten percent. </p>

<p>Janklow made state government more efficient by managing it like a business. He has
re-negotiated state contracts to make them less costly to the taxpayer, promoted joint
ventures with city and county governments to prevent local tax increases and eliminated
over 60 state government newsletters. He has also reduced the amount of overtime allowed,
consolidated state inspection programs, and privatized home health care. </p>

<p>Janklow also put state prison inmates to work on several building and remodeling
projects, saving millions of dollars for taxpayers. Janklow also created the only program
in America where prisoners build affordable homes for senior citizens who want to stay
independent and live in South Dakota's small towns. </p>

<p>Janklow's changes in law and administration have fixed workers' compensation problems.
He has also created hundreds of new higher paying jobs by bringing new companies to South
Dakota and helping the state's homegrown businesses grow even faster. </p>

<p>At the end of Janklow's eight years as Governor, one citizen told the Minneapolis
Tribune, &quot;We need someone as outspoken and animated as Janklow.&quot; State Senator
George Shanard told a Nebraska newspaper that Janklow's &quot;extremely aggressive,
extremely intelligent, extremely sincere. He's probably regarded as one of the best--if
not the best--governors in South Dakota history.&quot; </p>

<p>A daily newspaper editor wrote &quot;more often than not, he is a people's governor who
wants to make a difference for the people of his state.&quot; Another newspaper concluded,
&quot;The epitaph of his eight-year administration must read--what he did he did with the
honesty and courage of convictions. Call it dedication, call it sacrifice or call it
whatever you like, Governor Janklow has been good for South Dakota.&quot; 
<!--mstheme--></font><!--msnavigation--></td></tr><!--msnavigation--></table></body>
</html>

<p align="center"><img src="images/bio.gif" alt="bio.jpg (11504 bytes)" WIDTH="275" HEIGHT="88"></p>

<p><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Carole Hillard<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> is the first woman in the 106 year history of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>South Dakota<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> to serve as
the state's <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>.<br>
<br>
But, public service at both the local and state level isn't new to her.<br>
<br>
Before serving in the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>State House of Representatives<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> from 1991 through 1994, Carole
Hillard was a local and state leader in many different organizations.<br>
<br>
For seven years, she was a member of the City Council for Rapid City and served as its
first woman President. She has also been the president of the Rapid City Chamber of
Commerce and the Rapid City United Way Campaign.<br>
<br>
She has also served on the executive boards of the National Crime Prevention Council, the
South Dakota Municipal League, the West River Food Bank and Rapid City's Big Brothers I
Big Sisters organization. She has also been a member of the board of directors for the
National Crime Prevention Council, Heifer International, Michigan National Bank&nbsp; and
the Black Hills Eye Institute.<br>
<br>
In service to all South Dakotans, she has been the president or chairperson of several
statewide groups, including the Children's Home Society, the Corrections Commission, the
Governor's Crime Commission and the Board of Charities and Corrections.<br>
<br>
Lieutenant Governor Hillard has also been active as an organization officer for the Rapid
City Regional Hospital Steering Committee, Women Against Violence, the South Dakota
Commission on the Status of Women, National College, the Ellsworth Air Force Base Action
Committee, the Rapid City Downtown Development Foundation, the South Dakota Public
Assurance Alliance and the Rapid City Community Care Center and the Ninety-niners, an
organization of women pilots<br>
<br>
<TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Carole Hillard<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has volunteered to be an Election Supervisor in Bosnia
for the Peace Corps, Election Supervisor in Cambodia for the International Republican
Institute, Livestock Supervisor for Heifer International in Bolivia and Peru, and Election
Trainer in Angola, Africa for the International Republican Institute, Livestock Inspector
in Costa Rica for Heifer International and New Governor's Trainer in Nigeria for the
National Republic Institute.<br>
<br>
In 1986, she was recognized as the state's United Way Outstanding Chairperson. In the next
two years, she earned the Public Service Award and the Governor's Outstanding Citizen
Award. In 1993, she was named one of South Dakota's Outstanding Women. In&nbsp; 1999, she
was given the SD <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>Republican<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/> Party Abe Award.<br>
<br>
After earning a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>Bachelor of Arts degree in Education<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> in 1957, Lt. Governor Hillard was a
<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>school teacher<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>. She <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>operated a successful car dealership<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> and is a veteran member of the
South Dakota business community. The Lieutenant Governor also earned a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>Master's Degree in
Education<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> in 1983 and a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>Master's Degree in Political Science<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> in 1984.<br>
<br>
During legislative sessions, Lieutenant Governor Hillard is the presiding officer of the
South Dakota Senate. She also votes in the Senate whenever the votes cast are equally
divided. Outside the legislative sessions, she is concentrating her energies on global
concerns, elderly issues and improving child care opportunities in South Dakota.<br>
<!--mstheme--></font><!--msnavigation--></td></tr><!--msnavigation--></table></body>

    <td valign="top" colspan="2">
      <p></p>
      <p><a href="http://www.tennesseeanytime.org"><img src="../images/TNAnytime_logo.gif" width="140" height="68" border="0"></a></p>
      <p><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Don Sundquist<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was inaugurated as Tennessee's 47th governor in 
        January 1995. He was elected to a second term in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> with a record 69 
        percent of the vote. Since being in office, he has initiated unprecedented 
        reforms in the areas of welfare, crime and government, while placing a 
        special emphasis on <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Tennessee<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> children.</p>
      <p>Under his watch, the growth of state government spending has been more 
        than cut in half, allowing Governor Sundquist to invest in his administration's 
        priority areas:</p>
      <ul>
        <li>A safe, healthy start for children</li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
        <li>Excellence in education</li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
        <li>Economic opportunity</li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
        <li>Protecting public safety and health and the environment</li>
      </ul>
      <p>Governor Sundquist has worked on a bipartisan basis with the Tennessee 
        General Assembly to win approval for a wide array of programs that further 
        the priorities he has set.</p>
      <p>In 1996, Governor Sundquist won overwhelming bipartisan approval from 
        the General Assembly for Families First, a statewide welfare reform program 
        designed to move Tennesseans from welfare to work in 18 months. The program 
        offers job training and assistance with transportation and day care needs. 
        Since Families First took effect Sept. 1, 1996, Tennessee has seen a 60 
        percent reduction in the number of employable adults on welfare.</p>
      <p>Along with Families First, Governor Sundquist reformed the way Tennessee 
        cares for its children in need by consolidating all services under one 
        department. The move eliminates duplication of services, saves taxpayers 
        money and, most importantly, provides better care for needy and troubled 
        children.</p>
      <p>Governor Sundquist also hosted the first-ever Governor's Summit on Tennessee's 
        Children in June 1998 to bring together families, businesses, churches, 
        schools and volunteers to make a brighter future for Tennessee children. 
        His TNKids initiative, an outcome of the summit, stresses early intervention 
        and prevention services and coordination of services for families and 
        children at the state and local levels. </p>
      <p>In education, Governor Sundquist completed a six-year, $1 billion increase 
        in state funding to Tennessee schools through the Basic Education Program. 
        Through his ConnectTen project, Tennessee became the first state in the 
        nation to connect every public school and library to the Internet. To 
        protect school children from pornographic material on the Internet, Tennessee 
        also was the first state to implement software-filtering technology on 
        public school computers.</p>
      <p>Under Governor Sundquist's leadership, Tennessee has experienced four 
        consecutive record years of economic development, topping $5.4 billion 
        in capital investment in 1998. Since 1994, Tennessee has gained more than 
        186,000 jobs and personal income has increased by 13.3 percent.</p>
      <p>In health care, Tennessee led the nation by offering health insurance 
        to every child who otherwise has no access to coverage. The state's child 
        immunization rate is at an all-time high, while rates of teen pregnancy 
        and infant mortality are at record lows.</p>
      <p> </p>
      <p>A longtime advocate of strong law enforcement, Governor Sundquist promised 
        to work to make Tennessee safe. Keeping his word, he worked with the General 
        Assembly to win approval of four consecutive crime packages that crack 
        down on violent offenders, drunk drivers and juvenile delinquents.</p>
      <p>Governor Sundquist's environmental record captured headlines in 1998 
        when reports showed Tennessee's air, land and water were the cleanest 
        they've been in 25 years. The governor also has made protecting Tennessee's 
        pristine beauty a priority, adding 17 new state natural areas since taking 
        office.</p>
      <p>Governor Sundquist has appointed the most diverse Cabinet in history 
        and has named a record number of women to senior posts. He also has appointed 
        a record number of female judges. </p>
      <p>As a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>small businessman<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in Memphis, Governor Sundquist first ran for elected 
        office in 1982 after he and his wife, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Martha<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, had raised their three children. 
        Faced with an opponent who came from a famous Tennessee political family 
        and little name recognition of his own, Governor Sundquist defied the 
        odds and won the Seventh District congressional seat. He was re-elected 
        <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>congressman<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> five times by large margins of support from Republicans, Democrats 
        and independents.</p>
      <p>During his time in Congress, Governor Sundquist continually fought against 
        higher taxes and inefficient government. After a self-imposed term limit 
        of 12 years in Washington, he returned home to seek the governorship of 
        <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Tennessee<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/>, winning a hard-fought election that brought together Tennesseans 
        from all walks of life to support his &quot;In Touch with Tennessee&quot; 
        campaign. </p>
      <br>
      <hr>
      <font size="5">Don Sundquist<br>
      Governor of Tennessee</font><br>
      <p>Biographical information</p>
      <br>
      <p>Don Sundquist<br>
        <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Tennessee<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/><br>
        Profile</p>
      <p><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Don Sundquist<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was inaugurated as Tennessee's 47th governor in 
        January 1995. He was elected to a second term in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1998<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> with a record 69 
        percent of the vote. Since being in office, he has initiated unprecedented 
        reforms in the areas of welfare, crime and government, while placing a 
        special emphasis on Tennessee children.</p>
      <p>Under his watch, the growth of state government spending has been cut 
        in half, allowing Governor Sundquist to invest in his administration's 
        priority areas:</p>
      <p>A safe, healthy start for children<br>
        Excellence in education<br>
        Economic opportunity<br>
        Protecting public safety and health and the environment</p>
      <p>Governor Sundquist has worked on a bipartisan basis with the Tennessee 
        General Assembly to win approval for a wide array of programs that further 
        the priorities he has set.</p>
      <p>In 1996, Governor Sundquist won overwhelming bipartisan approval from 
        the General Assembly for Families First, a statewide welfare reform program 
        designed to move Tennesseans from welfare to work in 18 months. The program 
        offers job training and assistance with transportation and day care needs. 
        Since Families First took effect Sept. 1, 1996, Tennessee has seen a 60 
        percent reduction in the number of employable adults on welfare.</p>
      <p>Along with Families First, Governor Sundquist reformed the way Tennessee 
        cares for its children in need by consolidating all services under one 
        department. The move eliminates duplication of services, saves taxpayers 
        money and, most importantly, provides better care for needy and troubled 
        children.</p>
      <p>Governor Sundquist also hosted the first-ever Governor's Summit on Tennessee's 
        Children in June 1998 to bring together families, businesses, churches, 
        schools and volunteers to make a brighter future for Tennessee children. 
        His TNKids initiative, an outcome of the summit, stresses early intervention 
        and prevention services and coordination of services for families and 
        children at the state and local levels. </p>
      <p>In education, Governor Sundquist completed a six-year, $1 billion increase 
        in state funding to Tennessee schools through the Basic Education Program. 
        Through his ConnectTen project, Tennessee became the first state in the 
        nation to connect every<br>
        public school and library to the Internet. To protect school children 
        from pornographic material on the Internet, Tennessee also was the first 
        state to implement software-filtering technology on public school computers.<br>
        This year, Governor Sundquist has proposed a statewide reading initiative 
        to ensure that Tennessee children learn to read by the end of the third 
        grade. </p>
      <p>Under Governor Sundquist's leadership, Tennessee has experienced five 
        consecutive record years of economic development, topping $7 billion in 
        capital investment in 2000. Since 1994, Tennessee has gained more than 
        196,000 jobs and personal income has increased by 23.6 percent.</p>
      <p>In health care, Tennessee led the nation by offering health insurance 
        to every child who otherwise has no access to coverage. The state's child 
        immunization rate is at an all-time high, while rates of teen pregnancy 
        and infant mortality are at record lows.<br>
        <br>
        A longtime advocate of strong law enforcement, Governor Sundquist promised 
        to work to make Tennessee safe. Keeping his word, he worked with the General 
        Assembly to win approval of four consecutive crime packages that crack 
        down on violent offenders, drunk drivers and juvenile delinquents.</p>
      <p>Governor Sundquist's environmental record captured headlines in 1998 
        when reports showed Tennessee's air, land and water were the cleanest 
        they've been in 25 years. The governor also has made protecting Tennessee's 
        pristine beauty a priority, adding 23 new state natural areas since taking 
        office. </p>
      <p>In the new millennium, Governor Sundquist announced that for the first 
        time in over 50 years, Tennessee has a new State Forest, the Gulf Tract 
        in Cocke County. </p>
      <p>Governor Sundquist has appointed the most diverse Cabinet in history 
        and has named a record number of women to senior posts. He also has appointed 
        a record number of female judges. </p>
      <p>As a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>small businessman<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> in Memphis, Governor Sundquist first ran for elected 
        office in 1982 after he and his wife, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Martha<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>, had raised their three children. 
        Faced with an opponent who came from a famous Tennessee political family 
        and little name recognition of his own, Governor Sundquist defied the 
        odds and won the Seventh District congressional seat. He was re-elected 
        <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>congressman<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> five times by large margins of support from Republicans, Democrats 
        and independents.</p>
      <p>During his time in Congress, Governor Sundquist continually fought against 
        higher taxes and inefficient government. After a self-imposed term limit 
        of 12 years in Washington, he returned home to seek the governorship of 
        Tennessee, winning a hard-fought election that brought together Tennesseans 
        from all walks of life to support his &quot;In Touch with Tennessee&quot; 
        campaign. </p>
      <p></p>
      <p align="center">###</p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p>
      <p><br>
        Don Sundquist<br>
        Governor of Tennessee<br>
        Biographical Information</p>
      <p>Tennessee's 47th governor was born <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>March 15, 1936<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>. He married <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Martha 
        Swanson<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> in 1959, and they have three children and two granddaughters: 
        <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Tania (Mrs. David) Williamson<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> of Montgomery, Alabama; <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Andrea (Mrs. Art) 
        Jeannet<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> of Phoenix, Arizona; <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Donald Jr. (Deke)<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> of Nashville; Gabrielle 
        Renee Jeannet of Phoenix; and Alexandra Grace Jeannet of Pheonix. </p>
      <p>After graduating from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Augustana College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, he <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>served two years in the U.S. 
        Navy<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>. In 1962, he joined <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Josten's<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> and rose quickly to <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>plant manager<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> at 
        the scholastic products company's Shelbyville plant. Ten years later, 
        he struck out on his own, becoming <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>president and partner<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of Graphic Sales 
        of America, a Memphis printing and advertising firm. </p>
      <p>His political experience includes: National Federation of Young Republicans 
        chairman 1971-1973; Shelby County Republican chairman, 1976-1978; manager, 
        Howard Baker for President, 1979; first elected to U.S. Congress in 1982; 
        member, Ways and Means Committee, Subcommittee on Trade, Subcommittee 
        on Select Revenue Measures; vice chairman, Congressional Technology Assessment 
        Board; past chairman, House Republican Task Force on Trade; former member, 
        House Republican Task Force on Ethics Reform. He has received <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>honorary 
        doctorates<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Lincoln Memorial University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Union University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Newberry 
        College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>. He is a member of the Lutheran church.</p>
      <p><br>
      </p>
      <p align="center"><cite>Send comments to <a href="mailto:dsundquist@mail.state.tn.us">Governor 
        Don Sundquist</a></cite></p>

        Us</a></p>

    </td>

    <td valign="top" colspan="2"> 
      <blockquote> 
        <p><a href="www.tennesseeanytime.org"><img src="../images/TNAnytime_logo.gif" width="140" height="68" border="0"></a></p>
        <p><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Martha Sundquist<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> became the <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>First Lady of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Tennessee<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/> in January 1995 
          when her husband, <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Governor Don Sundquist<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> (R) was sworn in as the state&#146;s 
          forty-seventh Governor. Her continuing interests and activities have 
          centered on women&#146;s health issues, at-risk children and education.</p>
        <p>In 1996, Martha joined the organizing committee of America Walks for 
          Strong Women, a national event benefiting the National Osteoporosis 
          Foundation. She is also actively involved in raising breast cancer awareness. 
        </p>
        <p>As Tennessee&#146;s First Lady, she serves as an honorary member of 
          the National Advisory Council for Andrew Jackson&#146;s The Hermitage, 
          the University of Tennessee&#146;s College of Human Ecology and the 
          Tennessee Federation of Garden Clubs.</p>
        <p>Preserving and enhancing Tennessee&#146;s beauty is very important 
          to Martha. She works with the Tennessee Federation of Garden Clubs and 
          the Tennessee Department of Transportation on the state&#146;s wildflower 
          program, which showcases a variety of beautiful flowers on highways 
          and gateways throughout the state.</p>
        <p>The former Martha Swanson met Don Sundquist while both studied at <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Augustana 
          College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in Illinois. They married on <TAG name="DOM" value="start"/>October 3, 1959<TAG name="DOM" value="end"/>, after she had 
          graduated from college and he had completed his service in the Navy. 
          Martha was valedictorian of her high school class in 1955 and graduated 
          magna cum laude from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Augustana<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1959. While in high school and college, 
          she worked part time as a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>secretary<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> for the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Atomic Energy Commission<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> 
          and the A<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>rgonne National Laboratory<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>. After their marriage, Martha worked 
          for the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>John Deere Company<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> and the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Internal Revenue Service Center<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> in 
          Memphis from 1975 through 1981. She also has been active in a number 
          of church and civic organizations.</p>
        <p>During her husband&#146;s tenure as a U.S. congressman from 1982 to 
          1994, Martha was appointed by President Ronald Reagan to the USO World 
          Board, served as an officer in the Congressional Spouses organization 
          and the Congressional Club and was an active participant in the Congressional 
          Wives for Soviet Jewry.</p>
        <p>The Sundquists have three children: <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Tania Williamson<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> of Charlotte, 
          North Carolina; <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Andrea Jeannet<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> of Phoenix, Arizona and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Deke Sundquist<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> 
          of Nashville, Tennessee. They also have two granddaughters, Gabrielle 
          Renee Jeannet and Alexandra Grace Jeannet. In addition to spending time 
          with her family, Martha enjoys playing golf and gardening.</p>
        <p>Click <a href="1book-okl.htm">here </a> for information on the Executive 
          Residence. </p>
        <p align="center"><cite>Send comments to <a href="mailto:dsundquist@mail.state.tn.us">Governor 
          Don Sundquist</a></cite></p>

                        <TD WIDTH=38 HEIGHT=16><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=38 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>

                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD></TD>
                        <TD WIDTH=342><P ALIGN=CENTER><B><FONT COLOR="#990000" SIZE="+2" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT">Detailed BIOGRAPHY of <BR><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Michael O. Leavitt<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></FONT></B></TD>
                    </TR>
                </TABLE>
                <TABLE CELLPADDING=0 CELLSPACING=0 BORDER=0 WIDTH=461>
                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD>
                            <TABLE BORDER=0 CELLSPACING=0 CELLPADDING=0 WIDTH=260 NOF=LY>
                                <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                                    <TD WIDTH=10 HEIGHT=34><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=10 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>
                                    <TD></TD>
                                </TR>
                                <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                                    <TD HEIGHT=355></TD>
                                    <TD WIDTH=250 ALIGN=LEFT VALIGN=TOP><IMG ID="Picture141" HEIGHT=355 WIDTH=250 SRC="../assets/images/mol.jpg" BORDER=0 ALT="Governor Michael O. Leavitt"></TD>
                                </TR>
                            </TABLE>
                        </TD>
                        <TD>
                            <TABLE BORDER=0 CELLSPACING=0 CELLPADDING=0 WIDTH=201 NOF=LY>
                                <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                                    <TD WIDTH=16 HEIGHT=9><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=16 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>
                                    <TD WIDTH=179><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=179 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>
                                    <TD WIDTH=6><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=6 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>
                                </TR>
                                <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                                    <TD></TD>
                                    <TD WIDTH=185 COLSPAN=2><P><B><FONT COLOR="#000000" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT"><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Michael O. Leavitt<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/>,</FONT><FONT COLOR="#000000" SIZE="-1" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT"></FONT></B>
                                        <FONT COLOR="#000000" SIZE="-1" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT">
                                         the 14th <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Utah<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, has led the state through an era of change and unparalleled prosperity. Elected in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1992<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/>, reelected in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1996<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> with the largest vote total in state history and the second governor in Utah history to be reelected to a third term, Leavitt has carried out a vision of improvement and innovation while positioning Utah for success in a new millennium
                                        </FONT></TD>
                                </TR>
                                <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                                    <TD COLSPAN=3 HEIGHT=8></TD>
                                </TR>
                                <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                                    <TD></TD>
                                    <TD WIDTH=179><P><FONT COLOR="#000000" SIZE="-1" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT"> Crime is down, and student achievement is up. Open spaces are being preserved. Air pollution is 
                                        diminishing. Highways are expanding and welfare reliance is shrinking. In two terms, the Leavitt administration has met every state challenge while reducing property tax rates and cutting sales and 
                                        income taxes</FONT></TD>
                                    <TD></TD>
                                </TR>
                            </TABLE>
                        </TD>
                    </TR>
                </TABLE>
                <TABLE BORDER=0 CELLSPACING=0 CELLPADDING=0 WIDTH=466 NOF=LY>
                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD WIDTH=466 HEIGHT=4><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=466 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>
                    </TR>
                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD WIDTH=466><P ALIGN=LEFT><FONT COLOR="#000000" SIZE="-1" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT">. Under Leavitt, Utah has been named the "best-managed state" in America, the "best place to locate a 
                            business" and host of the 2002 Winter Olympics. <P>Governor Leavitt's leadership extends beyond the state's borders as well. He is past chairman of the National Governors' Association and a leading 
                            national voice on issues ranging from welfare reform and federal-state relations to e-commerce and balanced environmental management. <P>Born on <TAG name="DOB" value="start"/>February 11, 1951<TAG name="DOB" value="end"/>, in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Cedar City, Utah<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>, Leavitt graduated with a 
                            <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>bachelor's degree in economics and business<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Southern Utah University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and married <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Jacalyn Smith<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>. The governor and first lady are the parents of five children.<P>After earning his degree, Leavitt 
                            joined the <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Leavitt Group<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>, a regional insurance firm He eventually became <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>president and chief executive officer<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of the company, establishing it as one of the top insurance brokers in America. He also 
                            served as an <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>outside director of two large public corporations<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> and was a member of the Utah State Board of Regents, overseeing the state's nine colleges and universities. <P>Leavitt was successful in his first bid 
                            for public office, winning the governorship with 42% of the vote in a three-way race in 1992. He won reelection in <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>1996<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> with a record 74% of the popular vote. He is only the second governor in Utah history 
                            to be reelected to a third term. <P>At his first inauguration, Leavitt pledged to take the state to a "whole new level of performance." In the course of two terms, his vision of performance has 
                            become reality.<P>The average elementary class size in Utah is down by three students, while teacher salaries are up - all part of a 56% increase in overall spending for education in the Leavitt years.<P>
                            Leavitt education initiatives include the state's first charter schools, stricter graduation requirements and measures to guarantee reading proficiency, improve the education environment and bring technology to 
                            every classroom. <P>One in every four jobs that now exist in Utah was created on the Leavitt watch. Utah's traditional dependence on the defense industry has given way to diversification and an influx 
                            of high-tech industries.<P>Household incomes are rising and unemployment is at an all-time low.<P>Welfare reliance has fallen by more than half. More than 30,000 Utahns who previously had no health 
                            care insurance now have it as a result of Leavitt's Healthprint program launched in 1994.<P>Highways in Utah are being rebuilt and repaired at an unprecedented rate, including the largest design-build highway 
                            project in American history, a $1.6 billion total reconstruction of Interstate 15 through Salt Lake County.<P>Leavitt is a founder of Western Governor's University and creator of the Enlibra environmental 
                            management philosophy. <P>He negotiated the school trust lands swap with the federal government that secured millions of dollars for Utah school children; and he designed the "digital state" initiative 
                            that will deliver high-speed Internet access statewide and guarantee Utah's place in a global economy.<P>The governor has received numerous awards and honors and has been called on regularly by the president and 
                            congressional leaders to resolve federal issues that directly affect the states.<P>Leavitt embodies the hopes, dreams and beliefs of Utah, a youthful, energetic state. Asked once by a reporter how he would 
                            like history to remember him and the Leavitt years, he replied:<P ALIGN=LEFT><I>
                             "I'd like them to say Mike Leavitt was the governor that led us through a period of unparalleled growth and managed our obligation as a generation. That he helped us transition to the Information Age, and that our schools were better as a result. I'd like them to say that he oversaw a fundamental change in our philosophy regarding how we help people - that we began once again to help them as opposed to maintain them. And, most of all, that during the time he served, there was never a question that he was looking after our best interest."
                            </I></FONT></TD>
                    </TR>
                </TABLE>

                        <TD WIDTH=233><P ALIGN=CENTER><FONT SIZE="-1" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT"><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Lieutenant Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Olene S. Walker<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></FONT></TD>

                        <TD WIDTH=5 HEIGHT=11><IMG SRC="../clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=5 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>

                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD></TD>
                        <TD WIDTH=315  BGCOLOR="#FFFFFF"><P><BR><B><FONT COLOR="#003366" SIZE="+1"></FONT><FONT COLOR="#003366" SIZE="+2">Lieutenant<BR>Governor,<BR><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Olene S. Walker<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/></FONT><FONT COLOR="#003366" SIZE="+1">,</FONT>
                            <FONT COLOR="#003366" SIZE="-1"> <BR> the first woman <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>lieutenant governor of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Utah<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/><TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>, <BR> was born in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Ogden, Utah<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>. </FONT><FONT COLOR="#003366" SIZE="-1"
                             FACE="Times New Roman,Times,Times NewRoman">She obtained her <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>bachelor's<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>, <BR> <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>master's<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> and <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>doctorate degrees<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Brigham Young<BR> University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Stanford University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> and <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Utah<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>,<BR>
                             respectively.<P> From 1981 to 1988, Walker served as a member <BR> of the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>Utah House of Representatives<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, including serving<BR>
                             a term as assistant majority whip and majority whip. <BR> She founded and served as director of the Salt Lake <BR> Education Foundation. </FONT><P><FONT COLOR="#003366" SIZE="-1">
                             Under Governor Leavitt, she served as Chair of the<BR> Healthcare Reform Task Force that resulted in <BR>
                             establishing the Children's Health Insurance Program<BR> (CHIP). This provides every child in Utah access to <BR> medical insurance. She has served as chair of both the <BR>
                             National Conference of Lieutenant Governors and the<BR> National Association of Secretaries of State.</FONT></B></TD>
                    </TR>
                </TABLE>
            </TD>
        </TR>

            <TD WIDTH=608><P ALIGN=LEFT><B><FONT COLOR="#003366" SIZE="-1"> Lieutenant Governor Walker is currently leading Utah's battle against illiteracy. In conjunction with 
                Utah's Promise, 96 Community Literacy Teams have been trained and are actively engaged in giving the gift of literacy. <P> From 1969 to 1992, she served as the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>vice 
                president<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> of a family business, <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>Country Crisp Foods<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/>. She is married to <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Myron Walker<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/> and is the mother of seven children and 25 grandchildren.</FONT></B></TD>

            </TD>
            <TD>
                <TABLE BORDER=0 CELLSPACING=0 CELLPADDING=0 WIDTH=478 NOF=LY>
                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD WIDTH=4 HEIGHT=17><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=4 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>
                        <TD WIDTH=17><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=17 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>
                        <TD WIDTH=127><IMG SRC="../assets/images/auto_generated_images/clearpixel.gif" WIDTH=127 HEIGHT=1 BORDER=0></TD>

                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD COLSPAN=2></TD>
                        <TD WIDTH=248 COLSPAN=2><P><A HREF="../html/short_bio.htm"><B>Introductory Information</B></A><B></B></TD>
                        <TD COLSPAN=2></TD>
                    </TR>
                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD COLSPAN=6 HEIGHT=8></TD>
                    </TR>
                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD></TD>
                        <TD WIDTH=474 COLSPAN=5><P ALIGN=CENTER><B><FONT COLOR="#990000" SIZE="+1" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT"><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>First Lady<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> <TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Jacalyn S. Leavitt<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/><BR>Biographical Sketch</FONT></B><P><FONT COLOR="#000000"
                             FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT">Jacalyn Smith Leavitt is Utah's fourteenth <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>first lady<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>. As a result of her leadership, programs to encourage strong, healthy families have increased and volunteer efforts 
                            benefitting the state's youth have grown.</FONT><FONT COLOR="#000000"> </FONT><P ALIGN=LEFT><FONT COLOR="#000000" FACE="Arial,Helvetica,Univers,Zurich BT">Her concern for Utah's children has inspired her service. She 
                            developed the "Read to Me" public service announcement campaign, which promotes awareness and models ways parents can make reading more enjoyable for them and for their children. In addition, she wrote, 
                            "Read to Me," a children's story book, that is given to the parents of every newborn in the state to encourage them to read early and often with their children. In response to these literacy efforts, the Utah 
                            Library Association recognized her with the Promotion of Reading Award for 1999-2000. <P ALIGN=LEFT>Since becoming first lady, she has served as chair of the "Every Child By Two" Immunization Task Force. 
                            Eighty-two percent of <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Utah<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> two-year-olds are now adequately immunized against infectious diseases, an increase of nearly 20 percentage points from three years ago. The task force instituted the use of the Immunization 
                            Care-A-Van which provides nearly 7,000 free immunizations to Utah children each year. She teamed with Hallmark Cards to send a congratulatory card to new parents encouraging them to begin their child's series of 
                            immunizations. As a result of uniting the public and private sectors in this effort, she received the individual leadership award from the national "Every Child by Two" campaign.<P ALIGN=LEFT>Mrs. Leavitt is 
                            working with Utah's Promise, the statewide volunteer initiative, to encourage Utah's citizens to strengthen youth through volunteer programs. She hosted the televised GIFT of Literacy conference which significantly 
                            increased volunteer literacy efforts across the state.<P ALIGN=LEFT>As the spokesperson for the Children's Health Insurance Program (CHIP), she works to raise awareness among parents about available health insurance 
                            coverage for uninsured children. CHIP is a state sponsored health insurance plan for children whose families cannot afford private health insurance. Since the program started, more than 17,000 children have enrolled.<P
                             ALIGN=LEFT>As spouses'chair of the National Governors' Association, she spearheaded a national campaign to encourage pregnant women to quit smoking. She also serves as the spokesperson for "Baby Watch," a 
                            program for early detection of developmental delay in children. <P ALIGN=LEFT>She co-chairs GIFT, the Governor's Initiative on Families Today, which hosts conferences to strengthen Utah's marriages and families. She 
                            formed the Governor's Commission on Marriage--the first in the nation--to gather information on how society can create an environment for healthy marriages.<P ALIGN=LEFT>The first lady oversaw the two-and-a-half-year 
                            restoration of the Governor's Mansion. She enjoys showcasing this elegant, historic landmark to schoolchildren who visit it during their Utah history unit. In addition, every elementary school in the state has in its 
                            library an educational video highlighting the mansion and its history. <P ALIGN=LEFT>Mrs. Leavitt was raised in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Cache Valley, Utah<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/>, and graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Utah State University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> with a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in speech and elementary 
                            education<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>. She is a former <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>second grade teacher<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> at <TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="start"/>East Elementary<TAG name="PREVEMPL" value="end"/> in Cedar City. She is the proud mother of five children.</FONT><FONT COLOR="#000000" FACE="Times New Roman,Times,Times NewRoman"> </FONT></TD>
                    </TR>
                    <TR VALIGN=TOP ALIGN=LEFT>
                        <TD COLSPAN=6 HEIGHT=3></TD>
                    </TR>

		<TD ALIGN=left VALIGN=top WIDTH=2>
		</TD>
		<TD ALIGN=left VALIGN=top WIDTH=466>
		<TABLE WIDTH=466 BORDER=0 CELLSPACING=0 CELLPADDING=0>
			<TR>
				<TD ALIGN=left VALIGN=top WIDTH=466>
					<FONT FACE="Arial" SIZE=+1>
					<IMG SRC="images/dot_white.jpg" HEIGHT=6 WIDTH=1 BORDER=0 ALT="Office of the Governor"><BR>
					<IMG SRC="images/govmccallum.jpg" BORDER=0 ALT="The Governor"><BR>
					<P><TAG name="TITLE" value="start"/>Governor<TAG name="TITLE" value="end"/> Scott McCallum's Biography<BR>
					<IMG SRC="images/dot_white.jpg" HEIGHT=6 WIDTH=1 BORDER=0 ALT="Office of the Governor"><BR>
					</FONT>
					<FONT FACE="Arial" SIZE=-1>
					&nbsp;<BR>
					<B>Personal History:</B></P>
					<P><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>James Scott McCallum<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> was born on <TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="start"/>May 2, 1950<TAG name="DATEELECTED" value="end"/> in <TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="start"/>Fond du Lac, Wisconsin<TAG name="BIRTHPLACE" value="end"/>, the eldest of four children.  His father worked as an assembly worker at the Giddings & Lewis manufacturing company and later as a letter carrier, and served as president of his Letter Carriers Union.  Scotts mother was a homemaker and bank teller.</P>
					<P>Scott grew up in <TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="start"/>Fond du Lac<TAG name="GREWPLACE" value="end"/> and graduated from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Goodrich Public High School<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, where he lettered in four sports -- basketball, football, baseball and tennis.  Scott spent his summers working as a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>stock boy<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> at a local Sears store, a <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>lifeguard and swim coach<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/> at the neighborhood pool and unloading rail from gondola cars.  Through these experiences, Scott learned the importance of a good work ethic and small-town values.</P>
					<P>This commitment to hard work and sound values helped Scott make his way through <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Macalester College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in St. Paul, Minnesota.  To help make ends meet, Scott washed dishes in the school cafeteria.  He participated in three college sports -- football, swimming and baseball -- and served as captain of his college football team.  After graduating from Macalester College in 1972 with a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>B.A. degree in Economics and Political Science<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>, Scott earned a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>masters degree in International Economics<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Johns Hopkins University<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in 1974.  Scott then went to work in Washington D.C. as an <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>aide to the late Congressman William Steiger<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>. He later returned to Fond du Lac where he founded and managed a property development firm and served as a YMCA Program Director.</P>
					<P><B>Political History:</B></P>
					<P>In 1976 - at the age of 26 -- Scott McCallum ran for the State Senate seat, which represented his hometown of Fond du Lac.  He ran in the <TAG name="PARTY" value="start"/>Republican<TAG name="PARTY" value="end"/> primary against a 20-year incumbent and, in a stunning upset, he beat the incumbent by 32 votes.</P>
					<P>In the <TAG name="PREVPOS" value="start"/>State Senate<TAG name="PREVPOS" value="end"/>, Scott earned a reputation for strong, aggressive action, pushing for action on a variety of important state issues.  Scott also served for four years on the powerful Joint Finance Committee; five years on the Legislative Council and as one of six legislative members of the Joint Survey Committee on Retirement Systems. </P>
					<P>From 1976 to 1980, Scott was Chairman of the State Senate Campaign Committee, a period during which State Senate seats held by Republicans increased by almost 50 percent.</P>
					<P>In 1982, Scott won the Republican U.S. Senate primary with 72% of the vote.  In the general election against incumbent Senator William Proxmire, Scott won the third highest percentage of votes in the nation in that year against a Democratic incumbent.</P>
					<P>In 1986, Scott announced his candidacy for Lieutenant Governor and ran on a platform of restoring confidence in state government, revitalizing the states economy, and rebuilding confidence in the states ability to tackle any problem.  In the general election against incumbent Democratic Governor Tony Earl, Tommy G. Thompson and Scott McCallum emerged victorious.</P>
					<P>As Lieutenant Governor, Scott kept his promises and worked tirelessly to advance causes that he has described as being critical to the long-term quality of life in Wisconsin. </P>
					<P><B>Governor McCallum:</B></P>
					<P>After serving for 14 years as Wisconsins Lieutenant Governor, Scott McCallum was sworn in on February 1, 2001 as <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>Wisconsins 43rd governor<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/>.</P>
					<P>In his inaugural address, McCallum laid out a vision for state government, which included: lowering Wisconsins tax burden, improving education for all students, protecting Wisconsins environment, promoting a more efficient and effective state government, growing Wisconsins economy and helping the neediest in Wisconsin.  In his address, which was widely praised, McCallum said, "Its time for government to demand less, so citizens can do more for themselves and their families."
					<P>Three weeks later, McCallum delivered his first budget address to the State Legislature and followed through on the priorities he outlined in his inaugural address as he laid out his detailed spending proposals for the next state biennium.</P>
					<P>Despite facing a billion-dollar structural deficit, McCallums budget invested significant new amounts of money in public schools, higher education, health care, day care and economic development initiatives without raising taxes.</P>
					<P>McCallums budget contained the smallest state spending increases in 30 years and he proposed capping all future budget increases at the rate of growth in state personal income.  He also proposed a mechanism that would use any future state surplus funds for automatic income tax reductions and creation of a budget stabilization fund to help cushion the state budget against any economic slowdowns.</P>
					<P>During his first two months in office, Governor McCallum also finalized composition of his cabinet and traveled extensively throughout the state to reinforce his inaugural message and to explain his biennial budget proposals.</P>
					<P>On February 28, Governor McCallum nominated State Senator Margaret Farrow to succeed him as Wisconsins next Lieutenant Governor.  Farrow quickly won confirmation by the State Assembly and her confirmation is pending in the State Senate.</P>
					<P><B>Family:</B></P>
					<P>Scott is married to Laurie McCallum.  The couple has three children - Zachary, Rory and Cara.  Scott has also been active as a volunteer coach for youth sports teams; served on the Board of Directors for Wisconsin Special Olympics; served as State Chairman of the YMCA Youth in Government; and has remained a member of the Fond du Lac Rotary Club.</P>
					</FONT>
				</TD>
			</TR>
		</TABLE>
		</TD>
	</TR>
</TABLE>

					<FONT FACE="Arial" SIZE=+1>
					<IMG SRC="images/dot_white.jpg" HEIGHT=6 WIDTH=1 BORDER=0 ALT="Office of the Governor"><BR>
					<IMG SRC="images/MrsMcCallum.jpg" BORDER=0 ALT="Mrs. Laurie McCallum"><BR>
					<IMG SRC="images/dot_white.jpg" HEIGHT=6 WIDTH=1 BORDER=0 ALT="Office of the Governor"><BR>
					Meet the <TAG name="POSITION" value="start"/>First Lady<TAG name="POSITION" value="end"/><BR>
					<IMG SRC="images/dot_white.jpg" HEIGHT=6 WIDTH=1 BORDER=0 ALT="Office of the Governor"><BR>
					</FONT>
					<FONT FACE="Arial" SIZE=-1>
					<P><B>Professional Experience:</B></P>
					<P><TAG name="FULLNAME" value="start"/>Laurie McCallum<TAG name="FULLNAME" value="end"/> has, since 1982, been a Commissioner on the <TAG name="STATE" value="start"/>Wisconsin<TAG name="STATE" value="end"/> Personnel Commission.  This three-person, quasi-judicial commission is charged with deciding personnel and discrimination complaints filed by state employees.  For the past 13 years, Laurie has served as Chairperson of the Commission.  In this capacity, she has exercised primary supervisory and administrative responsibility for all commission employees.</P>
					<P>Prior to 1982, Laurie McCallum served as Executive Director for the Wisconsin Council on Criminal Justice; as Assistant Legal Counsel and Policy Advisor in the Wisconsin Governor's office; and as an attorney and project director in the Wisconsin Office of the Insurance Commissioner.</P>
					<P>Laurie has been a member of the Governor's Council on Judicial Selection - Supreme Court Vacancy - since June of 1993.  She has also served as an instructor at the University of Wisconsin School of Law and has been a member of the State Bar of Wisconsin since 1977.</P>
					<B>NOTE:</B>  Laurie McCallum has recently been appointed as one of three commissioners serving on the "Labor and Industry Review Commission".  She will assume these new duties on March 5, 2001.</P>
					<B>Education:</B></P>
					<P>Laurie McCallum began her undergraduate career at <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Macalester College<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in St. Paul, Minnesota.  It was during this year spent at Macalester College that Laurie first met Scott McCallum.  Laurie later transferred to the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>University of Arizona<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/>, in Tucson, Arizona, where she received a <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>degree in developmental Psychology<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/>.  Laurie McCallum received her <TAG name="DEGREE" value="start"/>Juris Doctor degree<TAG name="DEGREE" value="end"/> from the <TAG name="SCHOOL" value="start"/>Southern Methodist School of Law<TAG name="SCHOOL" value="end"/> in May, 1977.</P>
					<B>Personal:</B></P>
					<P>Laurie McCallum is married to Wisconsin <TAG name="SPOUSE" value="start"/>Governor Scott McCallum<TAG name="SPOUSE" value="end"/>.  They have three children:  <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Zachary<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>, <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Rory<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/> and <TAG name="CHILD" value="start"/>Cara<TAG name="CHILD" value="end"/>.</P>
					</FONT>
				</TD>
			</TR>
